\section{Honest status of the PDE}

The final target must be the PDE derived from the full complete TECT action.

However, the current derivation has not yet reached that final unconditional stage.
What is currently available is the strongest explicit working microscopic branch
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi],
\]
which is not yet claimed to be the final complete TECT action.

What is already closed is the reduced infrared Dirac form:
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

What remains open is the actual coefficient extraction from the final complete microscopic TECT operator:
\[
L(k)\ \to\ K_i\ \to\ P_*K_iP_*\ \to\ (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal final-complete TECT action ansatz consistent with all closed constraints}

\section{Goal}

The reduced Dirac theorem, the S2 transport structure, the Branch A / Branch B longitudinal audit,
and the remote-sector completion logic are already closed at the formal level.
What is still missing is not another reduction theorem, but a complete microscopic action
that contains every carrier slot required by those closed conditions.

Therefore we now write the \emph{minimal final-complete TECT action ansatz}
that is consistent with all already-established constraints.

\section{Closed constraints that the final action must satisfy}

The complete microscopic action must simultaneously satisfy the following facts already established
in the notes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the plain scalar Bragg route is insufficient;
\item the scalar identity-channel Bragg block is not cancelled inside the currently safe scalar library;
\item the relevant infrared carrier must therefore be a grading-odd first-order \(2+2\) block;
\item the actual local projector-defect geometry yields
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi));
\]
\item the natural reduced branch is S2:
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2);
\]
\item the transverse sector is controlled by \((\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\);
\item the longitudinal sector must realize either
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\quad\text{(Branch A)},
\]
or
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\ \lambda_c\neq 0
\quad\text{(Branch B)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the final complete action must contain enough microscopic carrier structure to generate:
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\qquad h_E(\theta),\qquad h_O(\theta),
\]
with at least one surviving admissible longitudinal seed and at least one nonzero transverse doublet seed.

\section{Minimal complete field content}

The minimal complete microscopic field content compatible with the closed constraints is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi(x,t)\in\mathbb C^3,
\qquad
P(x,t)=z(x,t)z(x,t)^\dagger,\quad z^\dagger z=1,
\qquad
X_i^a(x,t),
\qquad
\sigma(x,t).
}
\label{eq:final_ansatz_fields}
\end{equation}

Their roles are:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\Psi\): condensate triplet field;
\item \(P\): projector / orientational sector encoding the \(CP^2\) defect geometry;
\item \(X_i^a\): enriched Class II carrier field generating derivative witness transport;
\item \(\sigma\): heavy volumetric / amplitude sector needed for remote-gap structure.
\end{itemize}

\section{Minimal final-complete action ansatz}

The minimal complete action consistent with all closed logic is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\int dt\,d^3x\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
+
\mathcal L_{P}^{\mathrm{geom}}
+
\mathcal L_{\sigma}^{\mathrm{vol}}
+
\mathcal L_{X}^{\mathrm{II}}
+
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:final_complete_action_split}
\end{equation}

We now specify each piece.

\subsection{Condensate core}

The condensate core must contain at least the locked Brazovskii-type shell-forming piece:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
=
|\partial_t\Psi|^2
-\mu^2\,\Psi^\dagger\Psi
+Z\,\partial_i\Psi^\dagger\partial_i\Psi
-Y\,(\nabla^2\Psi)^\dagger(\nabla^2\Psi)
-u(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^2
+\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_core}
\end{equation}

The role of \(\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}\) is crucial:
it contains the still-undetermined complete microscopic refined derivative terms that may generate
a genuine constant-leading longitudinal Branch A coefficient
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0.
\]

\subsection{Projector / geometry sector}

The projector sector must encode the actual local \(CP^2\) defect geometry:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{P}^{\mathrm{geom}}
=
\frac{\kappa_P}{2}\,\Tr(\partial_\mu P\,\partial^\mu P)
+
\sum_{n\ge 2} a_n\,\mathcal I_n[P,\partial P,\partial^2P,\dots].
}
\label{eq:final_complete_projector}
\end{equation}

The first term gives the basic projector stiffness.
The higher invariants \(\mathcal I_n\) represent the still-open even/odd microscopic geometric
operators that may contribute to the actual transport kernel
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

\subsection{Volumetric sector}

The heavy volumetric mode is included as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\sigma}^{\mathrm{vol}}
=
\frac12(\partial_t\sigma)^2
-\frac12 M_\sigma^2 \sigma^2
-\frac12 c_\sigma^2(\nabla\sigma)^2.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_sigma}
\end{equation}

This sector is needed for the remote spectral benchmark and for the wrong-internal splitting scale.

\subsection{Class II carrier sector}

The enriched Class II carrier sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{X}^{\mathrm{II}}
=
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^aX_i^a
+\mathcal L_{X,\mathrm{kin}}^{\mathrm{ref}}.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_X}
\end{equation}

The term \(\mathcal L_{X,\mathrm{kin}}^{\mathrm{ref}}\) collects any still-allowed kinetic or derivative
refinements of the heavy Class II field that are absent in the minimal explicit branch but may occur
in the full complete TECT action.

\subsection{Complete microscopic mixing sector}

The full complete mixing sector must contain, at minimum, the currently explicit Class II carrier couplings:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_mix}
\end{equation}

Here
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi),
\label{eq:final_complete_J}
\end{equation}
while \(K_i^a[P,\psi]\) denotes the projector-coupled enriched derivative current.

The extra mixing term \(\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}\) is not optional in principle:
it is the placeholder for all still-open full-complete TECT microscopic couplings that are invisible
in the strongest explicit branch but may be needed to realize the actual coefficient point of the complete theory.

\section{Field equations of the minimal complete ansatz}

Varying \eqref{eq:final_complete_action_split} gives the full microscopic PDE system:

\paragraph{Condensate PDE}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp}}}{\delta \Psi^\dagger}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-2u(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+\mathcal F_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}
+\alpha_X\,\frac{\delta(X_i^aJ_i^a)}{\delta\Psi^\dagger}
+\beta_X\,\frac{\delta(X_i^aK_i^a)}{\delta\Psi^\dagger}
+\frac{\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}}{\delta\Psi^\dagger}.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_Psi_PDE}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Projector PDE}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp}}}{\delta P}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\kappa_P\,\partial_\mu\partial^\mu P
+\mathcal F_P^{\mathrm{geom}}
+\beta_X\,\frac{\delta(X_i^aK_i^a)}{\delta P}
+\frac{\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}}{\delta P}
=0.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_P_PDE}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Volumetric PDE}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp}}}{\delta \sigma}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\partial_t^2\sigma-c_\sigma^2\nabla^2\sigma+M_\sigma^2\sigma
+\frac{\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}}{\delta\sigma}
=0.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_sigma_PDE}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Class II carrier equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp}}}{\delta X_i^a}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
M_X^2X_i^a
+\frac{\delta\mathcal L_{X,\mathrm{kin}}^{\mathrm{ref}}}{\delta X_i^a}
+\alpha_X J_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta_X K_i^a[P,\psi]
+\frac{\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}}{\delta X_i^a}
=0.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_X_PDE}
\end{equation}

\section{Bloch-reduced effective PDE}

Linearizing around the locked periodic background and passing to Bloch momentum \(k\), one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi P}(k) & H_{\Psi\sigma}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{P\Psi}(k) & H_{PP}(k) & H_{P\sigma}(k) & H_{PX}(k)\\
H_{\sigma\Psi}(k) & H_{\sigma P}(k) & H_{\sigma\sigma}(k) & H_{\sigma X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XP}(k) & H_{X\sigma}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:final_complete_Bloch}
\end{equation}

This is the actual complete microscopic Hessian whose shell reduction must be analyzed.

After integrating out the heavy remote sectors \((P,\sigma,X)\) or, more precisely, after taking the
Schur complement relative to the isolated low-energy shell carrier, the effective shell operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)
=
H_{\mathrm{low,low}}(k)
-
H_{\mathrm{low,rem}}(k)\,
H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)^{-1}\,
H_{\mathrm{rem,low}}(k).
}
\label{eq:final_complete_Heff}
\end{equation}

\section{Final reduced infrared PDE}

The shell-projected infrared principal symbol must still take the closed S2 form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{comp}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{comp}} p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^{\mathrm{comp}}(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^{\mathrm{comp}}(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:final_complete_A1}
\end{equation}

The complete microscopic coefficient point is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
(\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{comp}},\alpha^{\mathrm{comp}},\beta^{\mathrm{comp}}).
}
\label{eq:final_complete_coeff_point}
\end{equation}

\section{Final exact tasks}

The remaining complete microscopic closure problem is now exactly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the full Hessian \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)\);
\item extract the actual transport kernel \(V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))\);
\item compute
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)];
\]
\item if \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\), compute the primitive coefficient \(\lambda_c\);
\item compute the transverse coefficients \((\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\);
\item verify the final nondegeneracy condition
\[
\bigl[\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\ \text{or}\
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\ \lambda_c\neq 0)\bigr]
\quad\text{and}\quad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{Honest interpretation}

This ansatz is not yet the proved final complete TECT action.
It is the minimal complete microscopic action form that contains every slot required by the already-closed
Dirac reduction logic.

Therefore the frontier is no longer structural.
It is the explicit evaluation of the coefficient point of the complete action.

\section{Final Summary}

The final target is not the strongest explicit working branch alone, but the PDE derived from a
complete TECT action.

The minimal complete action ansatz consistent with all closed constraints is
\[
S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\int dt\,d^3x\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
+
\mathcal L_{P}^{\mathrm{geom}}
+
\mathcal L_{\sigma}^{\mathrm{vol}}
+
\mathcal L_{X}^{\mathrm{II}}
+
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
\Bigr),
\]
with field content
\[
\Psi,\qquad P=zz^\dagger,\qquad \sigma,\qquad X_i^a.
\]

Its microscopic PDE system consists of the coupled Euler--Lagrange equations for
\[
\Psi,\qquad P,\qquad \sigma,\qquad X_i^a.
\]

After Bloch linearization around the locked periodic background, the full microscopic Hessian is
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k),
\]
and the effective low-energy shell operator is obtained by the Schur complement
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)
=
H_{\mathrm{low,low}}(k)
-
H_{\mathrm{low,rem}}(k)\,
H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)^{-1}\,
H_{\mathrm{rem,low}}(k).
\]

The reduced infrared principal symbol must still be
\[
A_1^{\mathrm{comp}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{comp}} p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^{\mathrm{comp}}(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^{\mathrm{comp}}(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

Thus the final complete microscopic closure problem is reduced to extracting the coefficient point
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\]
equivalently
\[
(\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{comp}},\alpha^{\mathrm{comp}},\beta^{\mathrm{comp}}),
\]
from the complete background-dependent TECT Hessian.

So the true remaining task is not to invent a new reduced PDE form, but to insert the complete action
into the already-closed extraction formalism and compute the actual coefficient point.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal independent invariant slots for the complete mixing sector}

\section{Goal}

We now determine the minimal independent invariant content that must be allowed inside
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}
\]
so that the final complete TECT action can realize the already-closed reduced S2 symbol
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

The point is not to enumerate every imaginable coupling.
The point is to identify the smallest set of independent microscopic carrier slots required by the
already-established extraction formalism.

\section{What the extra sector must generate}

The final microscopic operator must produce a local transport kernel of the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
with invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:extra_target_M}
\end{equation}

Therefore the complete mixing sector must supply, at minimum, three nontrivial carrier channels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one longitudinal \(\sigma_3\)-type channel;
\item one transverse even doublet channel;
\item one transverse odd doublet channel.
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the extra sector must be able to generate the shell tensors
\begin{equation}
\hat n_i\delta^{a3},
\qquad
e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2},
\qquad
-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}.
\label{eq:extra_shell_basis}
\end{equation}

\section{Restriction from the graded principal symbol}

Only terms linear in the fluctuation and containing exactly one worldvolume derivative contribute
to the graded principal symbol.
Thus the first variations must have the normal form
\begin{equation}
J_i^{a(1)}[\eta]
=
\mathcal J_i^{a(0)}(\xi)\eta
+
\mathcal J_i^{a\mu}(\xi)(-i\partial_{y^\mu})\eta
+\cdots,
\label{eq:extra_J_normal}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^{a(1)}[\eta]
=
\mathcal K_i^{a(0)}(\xi)\eta
+
\mathcal K_i^{a\mu}(\xi)(-i\partial_{y^\mu})\eta
+\cdots.
\label{eq:extra_K_normal}
\end{equation}

Hence \(\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}\) only needs to enlarge the coefficient content of the
\((i,a)\)-carrier sector.
It does not need to introduce qualitatively new derivative order.

\section{Minimal independent invariant slots}

A minimal complete choice is to add exactly three independent invariant families:

\subsection{Slot L: longitudinal even carrier}

The first independent slot must be able to generate a longitudinal \(\sigma_3\)-type seed.
The minimal invariant representative is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_L
=
X_i^a\,\hat n^i\,\mathcal S_a[P,\Psi,\sigma],
}
\label{eq:slot_L}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal S_a\) is an internal adjoint scalar built from the background projector/condensate data.
Its role is to generate either:

\begin{itemize}
\item a constant-leading Branch A term \(h_\parallel(0)\neq 0\), or
\item the primitive Branch B commutator-square seed.
\end{itemize}

Thus Slot L is not yet tied to Branch A or Branch B specifically.
It is the minimal longitudinal carrier slot that must exist in the complete action.

\subsection{Slot E: transverse even doublet carrier}

The second independent slot must generate the even transverse structure
\[
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2.
\]
The minimal invariant representative is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E
=
X_i^a\,\mathcal E^{ia}[P,\Psi,\sigma],
}
\label{eq:slot_E}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal E^{ia}\) transforms as the even shell doublet tensor.

Its reduced projection must have nonzero overlap with
\begin{equation}
e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2}.
\label{eq:slot_E_overlap}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Slot O: transverse odd doublet carrier}

The third independent slot must generate the odd transverse structure
\[
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2.
\]
The minimal invariant representative is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^a\,\mathcal O^{ia}[P,\Psi,\sigma],
}
\label{eq:slot_O}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal O^{ia}\) transforms as the odd shell doublet tensor.

Its reduced projection must have nonzero overlap with
\begin{equation}
-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}.
\label{eq:slot_O_overlap}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal complete mixing ansatz}

Therefore the minimal complete extra mixing sector can be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\gamma_L\,\mathcal I_L
+
\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E
+
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O
+
\text{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:extra_mix_minimal}
\end{equation}
with three independent couplings
\[
\gamma_L,\qquad \gamma_E,\qquad \gamma_O.
\]

Then the full complete mixing sector becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\gamma_L\,\mathcal I_L
+
\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E
+
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O
+
\text{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:complete_mix_minimal}
\end{equation}

\section{Why exactly three slots are minimal}

The reason this is minimal is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduced S2 symbol has exactly one longitudinal traceless channel;
\item it has exactly one even transverse doublet channel;
\item it has exactly one odd transverse doublet channel.
\end{enumerate}

No smaller set can span all three independent reduced witness directions.
Any larger set is redundant at the level of first-order principal-symbol closure.

So the complete action does not need an arbitrary zoo of extra couplings.
It needs, minimally, one generator for each of these three carrier directions.

\section{Correspondence with the coefficient point}

After Bloch reduction and shell projection, the three extra slots contribute only through the
already-closed coefficient point:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
}
\label{eq:extra_coeff_point}
\end{equation}

More explicitly:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal I_L\) contributes to the longitudinal branch decision:
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
\stackrel{?}{\neq}0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\lambda_c\stackrel{?}{\neq}0;
\]
\item \(\mathcal I_E\) contributes to \(\Lambda_E\);
\item \(\mathcal I_O\) contributes to \(\Lambda_O\).
\end{itemize}

Therefore the microscopic completion problem is now compressed to the question:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{which actual complete TECT invariants realize the three slots }
\mathcal I_L,\ \mathcal I_E,\ \mathcal I_O?
}
\label{eq:extra_last_question}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal final-complete PDE statement}

With these extra slots included, the complete microscopic action is now organized as
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\int dt\,d^3x\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
+
\mathcal L_P^{\mathrm{geom}}
+
\mathcal L_\sigma^{\mathrm{vol}}
+
\mathcal L_X^{\mathrm{II}}
+
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
\Bigr),
\label{eq:extra_final_action}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}\) is given by \eqref{eq:complete_mix_minimal}.

The corresponding complete microscopic PDE is the coupled Euler--Lagrange system for
\[
\Psi,\qquad P,\qquad \sigma,\qquad X_i^a.
\]

After periodic-background linearization and shell projection, the infrared principal symbol must be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{comp}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{comp}} p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^{\mathrm{comp}}(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^{\mathrm{comp}}(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:extra_final_symbol}
\end{equation}

Thus the complete PDE search is no longer underdetermined in structure.
It is underdetermined only in the microscopic realization of the three invariant slots
\[
\mathcal I_L,\qquad \mathcal I_E,\qquad \mathcal I_O.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The complete TECT action does not need an arbitrary number of extra couplings.
To realize the already-closed reduced S2 Dirac structure, the extra mixing sector needs only
three independent invariant slots:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_L
\quad\text{(longitudinal carrier),}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E
\quad\text{(transverse even carrier),}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
\quad\text{(transverse odd carrier).}
}
\]

Hence the minimal complete extra mixing ansatz is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\gamma_L\,\mathcal I_L
+
\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E
+
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O
+
\text{h.c.}
}
\]

The full complete mixing sector is therefore
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\gamma_L\,\mathcal I_L
+
\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E
+
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O
+
\text{h.c.}
\]

After reduction, these slots contribute only through the coefficient point
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

So the complete PDE search is now compressed to one final microscopic question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{which actual complete TECT invariants realize }
\mathcal I_L,\ \mathcal I_E,\ \mathcal I_O?
}
\]

In other words, the structure of the final PDE is no longer the problem.
The remaining problem is the microscopic realization of the three minimal carrier slots.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Lowest-order invariant candidates for the three open carrier slots}

\section{Setup}

Let
\[
P=zz^\dagger,\qquad z^\dagger z=1,\qquad
\Pi_Q=\mathbf 1_3-P,
\qquad
\mathcal T_\mu:=i[P,\partial_\mu P].
\]
On the defect background, the shell-compatible odd transport kernel must take the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
with invariant decomposition
\[
\mathcal M^\mu
=
h_0\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Hence we need one microscopic invariant for each of:
\[
n^\mu\sigma_3,\qquad
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\qquad
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

\section{Slot L: lowest-order longitudinal candidate}

The already-closed primitive longitudinal source is the traceless commutator-square channel
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
\]
Therefore the lowest-order longitudinal invariant candidate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_L^{(2)}
=
X_i^a\,n^i\,
\Tr\!\Big[T^a\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\Big].
}
\label{eq:IL_lowest}
\end{equation}

On the defect background,
\[
\mathcal I_L^{(2)}
\sim
X_\parallel^3\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
After solving the heavy-field equation for \(X_i^a\), the induced odd transport piece becomes
\[
V^\mu_{(L)}(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
so this realizes the primitive Branch B slot
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

\section{Slot E: lowest-order transverse-even candidate}

The minimal transverse-even carrier must project to
\[
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2.
\]
The lowest-order projector/condensate candidate is obtained from one projector derivative and one tangent derivative:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)}
=
X_i^a\,
\Tr\!\big(T^a\mathcal T_i\big)\,
\Re\!\big(z^\dagger D_\parallel\Psi\big).
}
\label{eq:IE_lowest_raw}
\end{equation}

More invariantly, after restriction to the tangent bundle, this is equivalent to taking the even shell-doublet tensor
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)}
=
X_i^a\,\mathcal E^{ia},
\qquad
\mathcal E^{ia}
:=
\Tr\!\big(T^a\mathcal T_j\big)\,E^{ji}.
}
\label{eq:IE_lowest}
\end{equation}

On the defect background,
\[
\mathcal T_j\sim \theta'(\xi)\times(\text{tangent adjoint}),
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)}
\sim
X_i^a\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^{ia}.
\]
After eliminating \(X_i^a\),
\[
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
so this contributes to
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E.
\]

\section{Slot O: lowest-order transverse-odd candidate}

The minimal transverse-odd carrier must project to
\[
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2.
\]
The lowest-order candidate is the parity-odd partner of the previous tensor:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}
=
X_i^a\,\mathcal O^{ia},
\qquad
\mathcal O^{ia}
:=
\Tr\!\big(T^a\mathcal T_j\big)\,J^{ji}.
}
\label{eq:IO_lowest}
\end{equation}

On the defect background,
\[
\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}
\sim
X_i^a\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^{ia}.
\]
After eliminating \(X_i^a\),
\[
V^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
so this contributes to
\[
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]

\section{Complete lowest-order extra mixing sector}

Therefore the lowest-order extra mixing sector consistent with the already-closed S2 carrier structure is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra,\,LO}}
=
\gamma_L\,X_i^a n^i\Tr\!\Big[T^a(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\Big]
+
\gamma_E\,X_i^a\mathcal E^{ia}
+
\gamma_O\,X_i^a\mathcal O^{ia}
+\text{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:LO_mix_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the shell-adapted seed basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{33}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C_{ij}^{31}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{32}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j}.
}
\label{eq:LO_seed_basis}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

\section{Induced reduced symbol}

After integrating out \(X_i^a\), the induced local transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{LO}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Big[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Big].
}
\label{eq:LO_Vmu}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{LO}}(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:LO_A1}
\end{equation}

So the lowest-order complete closure condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:LO_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal final-complete PDE}

The corresponding minimal final-complete microscopic action is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp,\,LO}}
=
\int dt\,d^3x\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\mathrm{core}}
+\mathcal L_P^{\mathrm{geom}}
+\mathcal L_\sigma^{\mathrm{vol}}
+\mathcal L_X^{\mathrm{II}}
+\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
+\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra,\,LO}}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:LO_complete_action}
\end{equation}

Its Euler--Lagrange equations for \((\Psi,P,\sigma,X_i^a)\) define the minimal final-complete PDE system
compatible with all already-closed reduced constraints.

\section{Final Summary}

The lowest-order open carrier slots are realized by exactly three invariant candidates:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_L^{(2)}
=
X_i^a\,n^i\,
\Tr\!\Big[T^a(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\Big],
}
\]
which generates the primitive longitudinal seed
\[
V^\mu_{(L)}(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3;
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)}
=
X_i^a\,\mathcal E^{ia},
}
\]
which generates the transverse-even seed
\[
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a;
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}
=
X_i^a\,\mathcal O^{ia},
}
\]
which generates the transverse-odd seed
\[
V^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Thus the lowest-order extra mixing sector is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra,\,LO}}
=
\gamma_L\,\mathcal I_L^{(2)}
+
\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)}
+
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}
+\text{h.c.}
}
\]

After integrating out the heavy mediator \(X_i^a\), the induced local transport kernel is
\[
V^\mu_{\mathrm{LO}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\bigr].
\]

Therefore the reduced principal symbol is
\[
A_1^{\mathrm{LO}}(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
and the lowest-order nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

So the minimal final-complete PDE search is now reduced to evaluating the three couplings
\[
\gamma_L,\qquad \gamma_E,\qquad \gamma_O,
\]
equivalently the induced coefficient point
\[
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit elimination of the heavy Class II carrier}

\section{Lowest-order complete microscopic action}

Take the lowest-order complete microscopic action
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp,LO}}
=
\int dt\,d^3x\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\mathrm{core}}
+\mathcal L_P^{\mathrm{geom}}
+\mathcal L_\sigma^{\mathrm{vol}}
+\mathcal L_X^{\mathrm{II}}
+\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
+\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra,LO}}
\Bigr),
\label{eq:Xe_start_action}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_X^{\mathrm{II}}
=
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^aX_i^a,
\label{eq:Xe_LX}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra,LO}}
=
\gamma_L\,\mathcal I_L^{(2)}
+
\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)}
+
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\label{eq:Xe_Lextra}
\end{equation}

Introduce the total \(X\)-source
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J_{i}^{a,\mathrm{tot}}
:=
\alpha_X J_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta_X K_i^a[P,\psi]
+\gamma_L\,\mathfrak L_i^a
+\gamma_E\,\mathfrak E_i^a
+\gamma_O\,\mathfrak O_i^a,
}
\label{eq:Xe_total_source}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathfrak L_i^a,\qquad
\mathfrak E_i^a,\qquad
\mathfrak O_i^a
\]
denote the local operator densities corresponding to
\(\mathcal I_L^{(2)},\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)},\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}\).

Then the \(X\)-dependent part of the action is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_X^{\mathrm{tot}}
=
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^aX_i^a
+
X_i^a\,\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:Xe_LXtot}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact heavy-field elimination}

The Euler--Lagrange equation for \(X_i^a\) is algebraic:
\begin{equation}
\frac{\delta S}{\delta X_i^a}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
M_X^2 X_i^a+\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}=0.
\label{eq:Xe_Xeq}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:Xe_Xsol}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Xe_Xsol} into \eqref{eq:Xe_LXtot} gives the exact tree-level effective interaction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\,
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}\,
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:Xe_Leff_master}
\end{equation}

Thus the complete lowest-order effective action is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\int dt\,d^3x\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\mathrm{core}}
+\mathcal L_P^{\mathrm{geom}}
+\mathcal L_\sigma^{\mathrm{vol}}
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\,
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Xe_Seff}
\end{equation}

\section{Expansion of the induced effective interaction}

Expanding \eqref{eq:Xe_Leff_master},
\begin{align}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{2M_X^2}\,J_i^aJ_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{2M_X^2}\,K_i^aK_i^a
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,J_i^aK_i^a
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-\frac{\alpha_X\gamma_L}{M_X^2}\,J_i^a\mathfrak L_i^a
-\frac{\alpha_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,J_i^a\mathfrak E_i^a
-\frac{\alpha_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_i^a\mathfrak O_i^a
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_L}{M_X^2}\,K_i^a\mathfrak L_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,K_i^a\mathfrak E_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,K_i^a\mathfrak O_i^a
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\Bigl(
\gamma_L^2\,\mathfrak L_i^a\mathfrak L_i^a
+\gamma_E^2\,\mathfrak E_i^a\mathfrak E_i^a
+\gamma_O^2\,\mathfrak O_i^a\mathfrak O_i^a
\Bigr)
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-\frac{\gamma_L\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak L_i^a\mathfrak E_i^a
-\frac{\gamma_L\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak L_i^a\mathfrak O_i^a
-\frac{\gamma_E\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak E_i^a\mathfrak O_i^a.
\label{eq:Xe_Leff_expanded}
\end{align}

\section{Load-bearing first-order transport sector}

The graded principal symbol keeps only terms that are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item quadratic in the light fluctuations;
\item odd under \(\xi\mapsto-\xi\);
\item linear in one worldvolume derivative \(\partial_{y^\mu}\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore, among \eqref{eq:Xe_Leff_expanded}, the load-bearing piece is the projection of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff,lb}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,J_i^aK_i^a
-\frac{\alpha_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,J_i^a\mathfrak E_i^a
-\frac{\alpha_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_i^a\mathfrak O_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_L}{M_X^2}\,K_i^a\mathfrak L_i^a
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:Xe_lb_sector}
\end{equation}
to the shell-/defect-adapted tangent sector.

The dots indicate terms of the same schematic type that survive the oddness filter and contain
exactly one worldvolume derivative.

\section{Quadratic shell template}

At the shell-relevant quadratic level, the complete \(X\)-source has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}
=
\lambda\,m^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,C_{ij}^{ab}(D_j\psi)\xi^b
+
\ell\,L_i^a
+
e\,E_i^a
+
o\,O_i^a.
}
\label{eq:Xe_quad_source}
\end{equation}
Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(m^a\partial_i\phi_0\) is the shell scalar-gradient source;
\item \(C_{ij}^{ab}(D_j\psi)\xi^b\) is the enriched tensor source;
\item \(L_i^a,E_i^a,O_i^a\) are the shell-adapted representatives of the three extra slots.
\end{itemize}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Xe_quad_source} into \eqref{eq:Xe_Leff_master}, the cross term between
\(m^a\partial_i\phi_0\) and the enriched tensor source reproduces
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^aC_{ij}^{ab},
}
\label{eq:Xe_deltaN_repeat}
\end{equation}
which is the already-closed Class II induced enriched tensor.

Likewise, the cross terms with the extra slots give
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^{b,(L)}\propto -\frac{\lambda \ell}{M_X^2}\,m^aL_{ij}^{ab},
\qquad
\delta N_{ij}^{b,(E)}\propto -\frac{\lambda e}{M_X^2}\,m^aE_{ij}^{ab},
\qquad
\delta N_{ij}^{b,(O)}\propto -\frac{\lambda o}{M_X^2}\,m^aO_{ij}^{ab}.
\label{eq:Xe_deltaN_extra}
\end{equation}

\section{Seed-basis evaluation}

Take the shell-adapted seed family
\begin{equation}
m^a=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:Xe_m_seed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:Xe_C_seed}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma:=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J.
}
\label{eq:Xe_deltaABC}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\nu_\parallel\,\Gamma\,c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\nu_\perp\,\Gamma\,c_I,
\qquad
g_O=\nu_\perp\,\Gamma\,c_J,
}
\label{eq:Xe_gcgego}
\end{equation}
up to the nonzero shell/defect overlap normalizations \(\nu_\parallel,\nu_\perp\). This is the
strongest honest normalization extraction currently available. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{Local transport kernel}

In the local defect language, the induced mediator transport kernel is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3n^\mu\Sigma_3+\cdots
}
\label{eq:Xe_Vmed}
\end{equation}
and in the exact concrete Class II branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:Xe_coeff_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:Xe_A1_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal nondegeneracy condition}

Thus the lowest-order complete closure condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:Xe_nondeg}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Xe_nondeg_g}
\end{equation}

\section{Resulting effective PDE}

The effective lowest-order microscopic PDE is obtained by varying
\eqref{eq:Xe_Seff} with respect to the light fields only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{LO}}}{\delta\Psi^\dagger}=0,
\qquad
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{LO}}}{\delta P}=0,
\qquad
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{LO}}}{\delta\sigma}=0.
}
\label{eq:Xe_light_PDE}
\end{equation}

At the shell-/defect-reduced level, its principal part is exactly \eqref{eq:Xe_A1_final}.
So the heavy-field elimination has reduced the complete microscopic PDE search to the coefficient
extraction problem for the mediator-induced transport triplet
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

Integrating out the heavy Class II carrier \(X_i^a\) is algebraic:
\[
M_X^2X_i^a+\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
X_i^a=-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
\]

Hence the exact tree-level induced interaction is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\,
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\]

At the shell-relevant quadratic level,
\[
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}
=
\lambda\,m^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,C_{ij}^{ab}(D_j\psi)\xi^b
+\cdots,
\]
so the cross term reproduces the already-closed induced enriched tensor
\[
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^aC_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\]
For the shell-adapted seed family,
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\nu_\parallel\Gamma c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E=\nu_\perp\Gamma c_I,\qquad
g_O=\nu_\perp\Gamma c_J,
\qquad
\Gamma=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
}
\]

In the local defect language, the induced transport kernel is
\[
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3n^\mu\Sigma_3+\cdots
\]
and in the exact concrete Class II branch
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]

Therefore the reduced principal symbol is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

So after eliminating \(X_i^a\), the final remaining problem is just the coefficient extraction of
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O,
\]
equivalently
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Complete TECT realization of the effective Class II source on the defect background}

\section{Locked defect background}

Take
\[
\Psi_B(\xi,x_\parallel)=\phi_0(x_\parallel)\,z_B(\xi),
\qquad
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\]
with explicit representative
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi).
\]

The tangent fluctuation is
\[
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp.
\]

Write the low tangent mode as
\[
\eta(\xi,y)=\sum_{a=1}^2 \chi_a(y)\,u_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a(\xi)=f(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\]
and the shell/test mode as \(\psi(y)\).

\section{Microscopic currents}

Use the minimal complete TECT currents
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T_a(\partial_i\Psi),
\label{eq:CTECT_J}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T_a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:CTECT_K}
\end{equation}

On the defect background,
\[
\partial_i\Psi_B=
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,z_B
+
\phi_0\,\partial_i z_B.
\]
Hence the shell-gradient piece of \(J_i^a\) is
\begin{align}
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
&=
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
\bigl(
z_B^\dagger T_a z_B
+
z_B^\dagger T_a z_B
\bigr)
|\phi_0|
+
\phi_0^2\,
\bigl(
(\partial_i z_B^\dagger)T_a z_B
+
z_B^\dagger T_a(\partial_i z_B)
\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&=
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\,\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\phi_0^2\,\mathcal A_i^a(\theta,\theta'),
\label{eq:CTECT_J_expand}
\end{align}
where
\[
m_a(\theta):=z_B^\dagger T_a z_B,
\qquad
\mathcal A_i^a:=(\partial_i z_B^\dagger)T_a z_B+z_B^\dagger T_a(\partial_i z_B).
\]

Since \(\partial_i z_B\neq 0\) only in the normal direction \(i=\xi\),
the shell-gradient carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
=
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\,\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\delta_{i\xi}\,\phi_0^2\,\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta').
}
\label{eq:CTECT_J_carrier}
\end{equation}

Now
\[
\partial_iP_B
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr),
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\qquad
k_a(\theta):=\Tr\!\Bigl[T_a(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:CTECT_K_carrier}
\end{equation}

\section{Effective mixed source after eliminating \(X_i^a\)}

Integrating out \(X_i^a\) gives
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a.
\label{eq:CTECT_Leff}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:CTECT_J_carrier} and \eqref{eq:CTECT_K_carrier},
\begin{align}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
&=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta')
\Bigr]
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\,\mathcal O[\psi]
\nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
2(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\phi_0^2\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta')k_a(\theta)\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigr]\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:CTECT_Leff_expand}
\end{align}

Thus the complete TECT realization automatically splits into:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
\mathcal L_{\perp}^{(1)}
+
\mathcal L_{\parallel}^{\mathrm{prim}},
}
\label{eq:CTECT_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\perp}^{(1)}
=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\phi_0\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl[m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)\bigr]\,
\mathcal O[\psi],
\label{eq:CTECT_perp_piece}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\parallel}^{\mathrm{prim}}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\phi_0^2\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl[\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta')k_a(\theta)\bigr]\,
\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:CTECT_long_piece}
\end{equation}

\section{Transverse channel extraction}

The first piece is linear in \(\theta'(\xi)\). After tangent-bundle reduction,
\[
m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)
\quad\mapsto\quad
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_b\Sigma_b+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_b\Sigma_b.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:CTECT_Vperp}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:CTECT_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

\section{Primitive longitudinal extraction}

Now evaluate \(\mathcal A_\xi^a\):
\[
\mathcal A_\xi^a
=
(\partial_\xi z_B^\dagger)T_a z_B+z_B^\dagger T_a(\partial_\xi z_B)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
\Bigl(
e_1^\dagger T_a z_B+z_B^\dagger T_a e_1
\Bigr).
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta')k_a(\theta)\,\theta'(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)^2\,Q(\theta),
\]
for some scalar \(Q(\theta)\) valued in the adjoint-singlet contraction.

After tangent projection, the traceless quadratic commutator channel is
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3
\]
and therefore the primitive longitudinal transport is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:CTECT_Vlong}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:CTECT_lambda}
\end{equation}

\section{Final reduced principal symbol}

Combining \eqref{eq:CTECT_Vperp} and \eqref{eq:CTECT_Vlong},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:CTECT_Vfinal}
\end{equation}

Projecting onto the graded low modes gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:CTECT_A1final}
\end{equation}

Thus the complete TECT realization of the minimal Class II carrier yields the final reduced PDE data
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:CTECT_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\section{Closure condition}

The final nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:CTECT_nondeg}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the reduced Class II coordinates,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:CTECT_nondeg_g}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Using the minimal complete TECT currents
\[
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi+\mathrm{h.c.},
\qquad
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T_a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\]
and eliminating the heavy Class II field \(X_i^a\), one gets
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a.
\]

On the defect background,
\[
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
=
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta'),
\]
\[
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,\mathcal O[\psi].
\]

Therefore the effective source splits into:

\[
\mathcal L_{\perp}^{(1)}
\sim
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\phi_0\,\theta'(\xi)\,[m_a k_a]\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\]
which generates
\[
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\bigr],
\]
and hence
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O;
\]

and

\[
\mathcal L_{\parallel}^{\mathrm{prim}}
\sim
\phi_0^2\,\theta'(\xi)\,[\mathcal A_\xi^a k_a]\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\]
which reduces to the primitive commutator-square channel
\[
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

Thus the complete TECT realization of the minimal Class II carrier yields the final reduced symbol
\[
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

So the final closure condition is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit shell/test-mode realization of \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal O[\psi]$}{O[psi]}}

\section{Minimal shell/test mode}

Let the shell/test mode be the complex transverse field
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\psi(y)=u_1(y)+i\,u_2(y),
}
\label{eq:Opsi_psi}
\end{equation}
where \((u_1,u_2)\) are the two transverse components on the polarization plane
\[
\hat k^\perp=\mathrm{span}\{e_1,e_2\}.
\]
The natural first-order test-mode operator is the worldvolume covariant derivative
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_j[\psi]=D_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:Opsi_Dpsi}
\end{equation}

This is the unique lowest-order choice compatible with the already-closed shell target form
\[
(\partial_i\phi_0)(\mathcal D_j\psi)\,\xi_a.
\]

\section{Minimal complete projector current}

We therefore choose the complete lowest-order projector/test-mode current in the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T^a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal T_j\,D_j\psi,
}
\label{eq:Opsi_K_general}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal T_j\) is a shell tensor acting on the transverse worldvolume derivative index.

To realize the S2 branch, \(\mathcal T_j\) must split into even and odd transverse parts.
Thus the minimal decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_j
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E_j
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J_j,
}
\label{eq:Opsi_T_split}
\end{equation}
where \(E_j\) and \(J_j\) are the shell-adapted even/odd transverse tensors.

Equivalently, in index form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T^a\partial_iP)\,
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j{}^{b}
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j{}^{b}
\Bigr)
D_j\psi_b.
}
\label{eq:Opsi_K_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{Defect-background insertion}

On the defect background,
\[
\partial_iP_B
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger),
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
\Tr(T^a\partial_iP_B)
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta),
\qquad
k_a(\theta):=
\Tr\!\Big[T^a(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)\Big].
\label{eq:Opsi_katheta}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit defect realization becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j{}^{b}
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j{}^{b}
\Bigr)
D_j\psi_b.
}
\label{eq:Opsi_K_defect}
\end{equation}

\section{Induced mixed term}

After eliminating the heavy mediator,
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a.
\]
Using
\[
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
=
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta'),
\]
with
\[
m_a(\theta)=z_B^\dagger T_a z_B,
\]
the shell-gradient contribution to the mixed term is
\begin{align}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff},\perp}^{(II)}
&=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\phi_0\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)\,
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j{}^{b}
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j{}^{b}
\Bigr)
D_j\psi_b.
\label{eq:Opsi_Leff_perp}
\end{align}

Thus the induced transverse transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:Opsi_Vperp}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal N_E,
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal N_O,
}
\label{eq:Opsi_LambdaEO_raw}
\end{equation}
with microscopic overlap coefficients
\begin{equation}
\mathcal N_E
:=
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\phi_0\,
m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\mathcal N_O
:=
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\phi_0\,
m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\label{eq:Opsi_NE_NO}
\end{equation}

After projection onto the low modes \(u_a^\pm(\xi)\), this gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:Opsi_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

\section{Longitudinal primitive branch}

The remaining term
\[
\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta')
\]
contracts with the same \(K_i^a\) and produces the primitive commutator-square channel.
Indeed,
\[
\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta')k_a(\theta)\,\theta'(\xi)
\sim
\theta'(\xi)^2,
\]
and after tangent projection,
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Opsi_Vparallel}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:Opsi_lambda}
\end{equation}

\section{Final reduced symbol}

Combining the two sectors,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:Opsi_final_A1}
\end{equation}

So the complete shell/test-mode realization is obtained by the minimal choice
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal O_j[\psi]=D_j\psi,
\qquad
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T^a\partial_iP)\,
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)\,D_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:Opsi_final_choice}
\end{equation}

The final nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:Opsi_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The minimal complete shell/test-mode choice is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal O_j[\psi]=D_j\psi.
}
\]

Accordingly, the lowest-order projector/test-mode current is
\[
\boxed{
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T^a\partial_iP)\,
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)\,D_j\psi.
}
\]

On the defect background,
\[
\partial_iP_B=\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger),
\]
so
\[
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\,
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)\,D_j\psi.
\]

After eliminating the heavy mediator, the mixed term
\[
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a
\]
splits automatically into:

\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl[
\Lambda_EE^\mu{}_a\sigma_a+\Lambda_OJ^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\bigr],
}
\]
hence
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\]
and

\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\]
hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

Therefore the final reduced principal symbol is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

So the remaining microscopic task is only to determine the actual signs and nonvanishing of
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O
\]
inside the full complete TECT action. This is exactly the currently honest frontier. 

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Nonvanishing criteria for the final reduced coefficients}

\section{Complete reduced symbol}

The reduced principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:NV_A1}
\end{equation}

Since the explicit defect profile already gives
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
the exact nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:NV_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{Coefficient extraction in the shell-seed basis}

Let the microscopic transport seed space be
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\},
\]
with
\[
B_\parallel\leftrightarrow \hat n_i\delta^{a3},
\qquad
B_I\leftrightarrow e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2},
\qquad
B_J\leftrightarrow -e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}.
\]

In the canonical Class II basis, the transport-response matrix is diagonal:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{diag}(\mu_\parallel,\mu_I,\mu_J),
\qquad
\mu_\parallel\neq 0,\quad
\mu_I\neq 0,\quad
\mu_J\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:NV_seed_diag}
\end{equation}

For a general seed combination
\begin{equation}
N
=
c_\parallel B_\parallel
+
c_I B_I
+
c_J B_J,
\label{eq:NV_seed_comb}
\end{equation}
the reduced coefficients are therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\mu_\parallel c_\parallel,
\qquad
\Lambda_E=\mu_I c_I,
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mu_J c_J.
}
\label{eq:NV_seed_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Hence the sign information is immediate:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_c)=\operatorname{sgn}(\mu_\parallel)\operatorname{sgn}(c_\parallel),
\quad
\operatorname{sgn}(\Lambda_E)=\operatorname{sgn}(\mu_I)\operatorname{sgn}(c_I),
\quad
\operatorname{sgn}(\Lambda_O)=\operatorname{sgn}(\mu_J)\operatorname{sgn}(c_J).
}
\label{eq:NV_signs}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal nonvanishing theorem}

Let \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) denote the actual microscopic transport space produced by the full complete TECT action.
Let
\[
P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}
\]
be the orthogonal projection onto that space.

Then the exact finite completion criterion is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:NV_long_criterion}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_I\neq 0
\ \text{or}\
P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_J\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:NV_trans_criterion}
\end{equation}

Therefore a sufficient condition for the full reduced symbol to be nondegenerate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_I,\ P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_J\bigr)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:NV_full_projection}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:NV_full_projection}, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:NV_full_nondeg}
\end{equation}
hence by \eqref{eq:NV_A1},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)\ \text{is Dirac-nondegenerate.}
}
\label{eq:NV_Dirac_done}
\end{equation}

\section{Direct coefficient formulas from the chosen complete realization}

For the chosen lowest-order complete realization
\[
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T^a\partial_iP)\,
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)\,D_j\psi,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a,
\]
the reduced coefficients take the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal N_E,
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal N_O,
}
\label{eq:NV_EO_formula}
\end{equation}
for microscopic overlaps \(\mathcal N_E,\mathcal N_O\), and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal N_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:NV_L_formula}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal N_\parallel\) is the primitive commutator-square overlap.

Thus the practical sufficient conditions are simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal N_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\mathcal N_E,\mathcal N_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:NV_overlap_condition}
\end{equation}

If \(\alpha\beta\neq 0\), then \eqref{eq:NV_overlap_condition} implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:NV_overlap_implies}
\end{equation}

\section{Final complete-PDE criterion}

Therefore the complete TECT PDE closes at lowest order iff the full microscopic Hessian generates
nonzero overlap with the three shell target directions:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal N_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\mathcal N_E,\mathcal N_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:NV_final_complete}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the seed-language,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:NV_seed_final}
\end{equation}

Then the final reduced PDE is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:NV_final_PDE}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The final reduced PDE is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

Since
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
its exact nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

In the canonical Class II seed basis,
\[
\lambda_c=\mu_\parallel c_\parallel,
\qquad
\Lambda_E=\mu_I c_I,
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mu_J c_J,
\]
with
\[
\mu_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad
\mu_I\neq 0,\qquad
\mu_J\neq 0.
\]

Therefore a sufficient microscopic completion criterion is
\[
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_I,\ P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}B_J\bigr)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

For the chosen complete realization,
\[
\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\mathcal N_E,
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\mathcal N_O,
\qquad
\lambda_c
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\mathcal N_\parallel.
\]

So the entire final complete-PDE problem is reduced to the three overlap tests
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\mathcal N_E,\mathcal N_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit evaluation of \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal N_\parallel,\mathcal N_E,\mathcal N_O$}{N_parallel,N_E,N_O} for a concrete generator choice}

\section{Concrete embedded \texorpdfstring{$SU(2)$}{SU(2)} choice}

Choose the embedded \(SU(2)\) acting on the \((1,3)\)-plane:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_1=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&1\\
0&0&0\\
1&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T_2=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&-i\\
0&0&0\\
i&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T_3=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&0&0\\
0&0&-1
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:NEO_Tchoice}
\end{equation}

Take the explicit real defect representative
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:NEO_z_choice}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi).
\]

\section{Basic adjoint contractions}

Define
\begin{equation}
m_a(\theta):=z_B^\dagger T_a z_B,
\label{eq:NEO_mdef}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
k_a(\theta):=\Tr\!\Big[T_a(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)\Big],
\label{eq:NEO_kdef}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
A_a(\theta):=
e_1^\dagger T_a z_B+z_B^\dagger T_a e_1.
\label{eq:NEO_Adef}
\end{equation}

A direct computation gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_1=\frac12\sin 2\theta,
\qquad
m_2=0,
\qquad
m_3=\frac12\cos 2\theta,
}
\label{eq:NEO_mvals}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_1=\cos 2\theta,
\qquad
k_2=0,
\qquad
k_3=-\sin 2\theta,
}
\label{eq:NEO_kvals}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1=\cos 2\theta,
\qquad
A_2=0,
\qquad
A_3=-\sin 2\theta.
}
\label{eq:NEO_Avals}
\end{equation}

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_a(\theta)=k_a(\theta).
}
\label{eq:NEO_Aeqk}
\end{equation}

\section{Transverse overlap}

The transverse piece of the effective mixed current comes from the \(\theta'(\xi)\)-order term
\[
m_a(\theta)\,k_a(\theta).
\]
Using \eqref{eq:NEO_mvals} and \eqref{eq:NEO_kvals},
\begin{align}
m_a k_a
&=
m_1k_1+m_2k_2+m_3k_3
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac12\sin 2\theta\cos 2\theta
+
0
+
\frac12\cos 2\theta(-\sin 2\theta)
\nonumber\\
&=0.
\label{eq:NEO_mk_zero}
\end{align}

Therefore the minimal bare \(JK\) realization produces no transverse overlap:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal N_E=0,
\qquad
\mathcal N_O=0.
}
\label{eq:NEO_EO_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_O=0
}
\label{eq:NEO_LambdaEO_zero}
\end{equation}
for this minimal real representative.

\section{Primitive longitudinal overlap}

The longitudinal primitive piece comes from
\[
A_a(\theta)\,k_a(\theta)\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:NEO_Avals} and \eqref{eq:NEO_kvals},
\begin{align}
A_a k_a
&=
A_1k_1+A_2k_2+A_3k_3
\nonumber\\
&=
\cos^2 2\theta+0+(-\sin 2\theta)(-\sin 2\theta)
\nonumber\\
&=
1.
\label{eq:NEO_Ak_one}
\end{align}

Thus the primitive longitudinal overlap is strictly nonzero:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal N_\parallel=1
}
\label{eq:NEO_Nparallel_one}
\end{equation}
up to the overall shell/defect normalization conventions.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal N_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\neq 0
\qquad
(\alpha\beta\neq 0).
}
\label{eq:NEO_lambdac_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{2M_X^2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:NEO_lambdaparallel}
\end{equation}

\section{Resulting reduced symbol}

For this minimal real complete realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{2M_X^2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:NEO_A1_longonly}
\end{equation}

So the reduced symbol is longitudinal-only and fails full Dirac nondegeneracy:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O=0.
}
\label{eq:NEO_final_result}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate consequence}

Therefore the complete microscopic conclusion is sharp:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the minimal bare }J_i^aK_i^a\text{ realization on the real }CP^2\text{ representative closes the primitive longitudinal channel,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{it does not generate the transverse-even or transverse-odd channels.}
}
\end{equation}

Hence the full complete TECT action must contain additional transverse carrier structure, namely the
extra \(E/O\)-slots previously identified:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E,\qquad \mathcal I_O.
}
\label{eq:NEO_need_extra}
\end{equation}

Without them, the final reduced PDE is not fully Dirac-nondegenerate.

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit generator choice
\[
T_1=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&1\\
0&0&0\\
1&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\quad
T_2=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&-i\\
0&0&0\\
i&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\quad
T_3=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&0&0\\
0&0&-1
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and the real defect representative
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one finds
\[
m_1=\frac12\sin 2\theta,\qquad m_2=0,\qquad m_3=\frac12\cos 2\theta,
\]
\[
k_1=\cos 2\theta,\qquad k_2=0,\qquad k_3=-\sin 2\theta,
\]
\[
A_1=\cos 2\theta,\qquad A_2=0,\qquad A_3=-\sin 2\theta.
\]

Hence
\[
m_a k_a=0,
\]
so the transverse overlaps vanish:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_E=0,\qquad \mathcal N_O=0.
}
\]

But
\[
A_a k_a=1,
\]
so the primitive longitudinal overlap is nonzero:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_\parallel=1.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c=-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\neq 0
\quad(\alpha\beta\neq 0),
\qquad
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O=0.
}
\]

Thus the minimal bare \(J_i^aK_i^a\) realization on the real \(CP^2\) representative produces only the
primitive longitudinal channel and does not generate the transverse Dirac channels.

So the full complete TECT action must contain additional transverse carrier slots \(\mathcal I_E,\mathcal I_O\)
if the final reduced PDE is to be fully Dirac-nondegenerate.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit transverse completion by extra \(E/O\) slots}

\section{Defect frame}

Keep the same real defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:EO_zbasis}
\end{equation}

Thus
\[
Q_B(\xi)=\mathrm{span}\{e_1(\xi),e_2\}.
\]

\section{Why the previous minimal realization failed}

With the embedded \(SU(2)_{(13)}\) generators
\[
T_1,T_2,T_3,
\]
all adjoint contractions only saw the \((1,3)\)-plane. Hence the contraction
\[
m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)
\]
cancelled identically, giving
\[
\mathcal N_E=\mathcal N_O=0,
\]
while the primitive longitudinal contraction
\[
A_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)=1
\]
survived. Therefore the transverse slots must involve generators that see the second tangent vector \(e_2\).

\section{Minimal transverse generator pair}

Choose the lowest-order Hermitian pair mixing the \((1,2)\)-plane:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_E:=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1&0\\
1&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
S_O:=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i&0\\
i&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:EO_generators}
\end{equation}

These are the minimal extra generators needed to couple \(z_B\) to \(e_2\).

\section{Even transverse carrier}

Define the even transverse rank-one projector tensor
\begin{equation}
M_E:=e_2 z_B^\dagger+z_B e_2^\dagger.
\label{eq:EO_ME}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:EO_zbasis},
\begin{equation}
M_E=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&\cos\theta&0\\
\cos\theta&0&\sin\theta\\
0&\sin\theta&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:EO_ME_explicit}
\end{equation}

Now compute
\begin{equation}
q_E(\theta):=\Tr(S_E M_E).
\label{eq:EO_qE_def}
\end{equation}
Since
\[
\Tr(S_E M_E)=\frac12(M_{12}+M_{21}),
\]
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_E(\theta)=\cos\theta.
}
\label{eq:EO_qE}
\end{equation}

Therefore the lowest-order even extra slot
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E
=
X_i^{(E)}\,\Tr(S_E M_E)\,E_j D_j\psi
=
X_i^{(E)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,E_j D_j\psi
}
\label{eq:EO_IE}
\end{equation}
is nonzero on the defect background whenever \(\cos\theta\not\equiv 0\).

\section{Odd transverse carrier}

Define the odd transverse rank-one tensor
\begin{equation}
M_O:=i(e_2 z_B^\dagger-z_B e_2^\dagger).
\label{eq:EO_MO}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:EO_zbasis},
\begin{equation}
M_O=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i\cos\theta&0\\
i\cos\theta&0&-i\sin\theta\\
0&i\sin\theta&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:EO_MO_explicit}
\end{equation}

Now compute
\begin{equation}
q_O(\theta):=\Tr(S_O M_O).
\label{eq:EO_qO_def}
\end{equation}
Since
\[
\Tr(S_O M_O)=\frac12(-i\,M_{21}+i\,M_{12}),
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_O(\theta)=\cos\theta.
}
\label{eq:EO_qO}
\end{equation}

Hence the lowest-order odd extra slot
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\Tr(S_O M_O)\,J_j D_j\psi
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_j D_j\psi
}
\label{eq:EO_IO}
\end{equation}
is also nonzero whenever \(\cos\theta\not\equiv 0\).

\section{Heavy-field elimination}

Include the transverse extra source
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_{i}^{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\gamma_E\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,E_jD_j\psi
+
\gamma_O\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
\label{eq:EO_Jextra}
\end{equation}

After eliminating the heavy field \(X_i\),
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\mathcal J_i^{\mathrm{tot}}\mathcal J_i^{\mathrm{tot}}.
\label{eq:EO_Leff}
\end{equation}

The shell-relevant cross terms give the transverse transport kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:EO_Vperp}
\end{equation}

Define the weighted defect overlap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta,\cos}:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:EO_Ithetacos}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_{\theta,\cos}\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_{\theta,\cos}\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:EO_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
\frac{d}{d\xi}\sin\theta(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta,\cos}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\frac{d}{d\xi}\sin\theta(\xi).
\label{eq:EO_Ithetacos_deriv}
\end{equation}
For a monotone defect profile with nontrivial \(\theta\)-variation and nonvanishing even-odd overlap \(f_+f_-\),
this is generically nonzero:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta,\cos}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:EO_Ithetacos_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal N_E=\cos\theta\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
\mathcal N_O=\cos\theta\not\equiv 0,
}
\label{eq:EO_NE_NO_nonzero}
\end{equation}
and consequently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E\neq 0,
\qquad
\Lambda_O\neq 0
}
\label{eq:EO_LambdaEO_nonzero}
\end{equation}
whenever \(\gamma_E,\gamma_O\neq 0\).

\section{Full reduced symbol}

Combining this with the already-established primitive longitudinal channel
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\lambda_c=-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\mathcal N_\parallel,
\qquad
\mathcal N_\parallel=1,
\]
the final reduced symbol becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:EO_final_A1}
\end{equation}

Hence the full nondegeneracy condition is satisfied:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:EO_full_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The minimal bare \(SU(2)_{(13)}\) realization gives only the primitive longitudinal channel.
After adding the explicit transverse extra generators \(S_E,S_O\), the transverse even and odd channels
become nonzero on the same defect background.

Therefore the complete lowest-order TECT realization is fully Dirac-nondegenerate.

\section{Final Summary}

Take
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and the extra transverse generators
\[
S_E=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1&0\\
1&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
S_O=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i&0\\
i&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then
\[
M_E=e_2z_B^\dagger+z_Be_2^\dagger,
\qquad
M_O=i(e_2z_B^\dagger-z_Be_2^\dagger),
\]
satisfy
\[
\Tr(S_E M_E)=\cos\theta,
\qquad
\Tr(S_O M_O)=\cos\theta.
\]

Therefore the extra transverse slots are explicitly nonzero:
\[
\mathcal I_E\sim X^{(E)}\cos\theta\,E_jD_j\psi,
\qquad
\mathcal I_O\sim X^{(O)}\cos\theta\,J_jD_j\psi.
\]

After heavy-field elimination, the induced transverse kernel is
\[
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\bigr].
\]
Hence
\[
\alpha=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O,
\qquad
I_{\theta,\cos}=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'\cos\theta\neq 0.
\]

Combining this with the primitive longitudinal channel
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\mathcal N_\parallel=1,
\]
the final reduced symbol is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

Thus, after adding the explicit extra transverse carriers, the complete lowest-order TECT realization
becomes fully Dirac-nondegenerate:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Final PDE Statement of the Lowest-Order Complete TECT Realization}

\section{Complete microscopic field content}

The lowest-order complete TECT realization contains the fields
\[
\Psi(x,t)\in\mathbb C^3,
\qquad
P(x,t)=z(x,t)z(x,t)^\dagger,\quad z^\dagger z=1,
\qquad
X_i^a(x,t),
\qquad
\sigma(x,t).
\]

\section{Complete lowest-order action}

The complete lowest-order microscopic action is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp,LO}}
=
\int dt\,d^3x\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\mathrm{core}}
+\mathcal L_P^{\mathrm{geom}}
+\mathcal L_\sigma^{\mathrm{vol}}
+\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
+\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E
+\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:FinalPDE_action}
\end{equation}

The microscopic currents are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T_a(\partial_i\Psi),
}
\label{eq:FinalPDE_J}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T_a\partial_iP)\,
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)\,D_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:FinalPDE_K}
\end{equation}

The extra transverse carriers are realized by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E
\sim
X^{(E)}\Tr(S_E M_E)\,E_jD_j\psi,
\qquad
\mathcal I_O
\sim
X^{(O)}\Tr(S_O M_O)\,J_jD_j\psi,
}
\label{eq:FinalPDE_IO}
\end{equation}
with
\[
S_E=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1&0\\
1&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
S_O=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i&0\\
i&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and
\[
M_E=e_2z_B^\dagger+z_Be_2^\dagger,
\qquad
M_O=i(e_2z_B^\dagger-z_Be_2^\dagger).
\]

\section{Microscopic Euler--Lagrange PDE system}

The full microscopic PDE system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp,LO}}}{\delta\Psi^\dagger}=0,
\qquad
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp,LO}}}{\delta P}=0,
\qquad
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp,LO}}}{\delta\sigma}=0,
\qquad
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{TECT}}^{\mathrm{comp,LO}}}{\delta X_i^a}=0.
}
\label{eq:FinalPDE_EL}
\end{equation}

The heavy-field equation is algebraic:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_X^2X_i^a+\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}=0,
\qquad
X_i^a=-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:FinalPDE_Xelim}
\end{equation}

Hence the induced effective interaction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:FinalPDE_LeffX}
\end{equation}

\section{Defect background}

Take the explicit defect representative
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}

\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad

\end{pmatrix}.

\end{equation}

Then
\[

\qquad

=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\]

\section{Effective transport kernel}

For the explicit transverse generators \(S_E,S_O\), one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Tr(S_E M_E)=\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\Tr(S_O M_O)=\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:FinalPDE_transverse_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Hence the effective mediator transport kernel is
\begin{equation}

+

\Bigr].

\label{eq:FinalPDE_Vmu}
\end{equation}

Define the defect overlaps

\begin{equation}

\qquad

\label{eq:FinalPDE_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\section{Final reduced infrared PDE}

After Bloch reduction around the locked 12-mode BCC background and shell projection at

the final reduced principal symbol is

Under these conditions, the lowest-order complete TECT realization is fully Dirac-nondegenerate.

\section{Final Summary}

The lowest-order complete TECT realization is the coupled microscopic PDE system for

derived from
