\paragraph{Branch A.}
If the complete microscopic TECT action realizes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:Honest_A}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\end{equation}
so the longitudinal channel is already present on the constant-leading branch.

\paragraph{Branch B.}
If instead
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:Honest_B}
\end{equation}
then the longitudinal channel is realized only through the primitive commutator-square seed,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:Honest_B_lambda}
\end{equation}

The exact concrete currently constructed Class II branch realizes Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:Honest_ClassII}
\end{equation}

Therefore the strongest explicit currently available reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{(B)}(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:Honest_current_PDE}
\end{equation}

However, this does \emph{not} yet prove that the final complete TECT action itself must lie on Branch B.
The true complete microscopic closure problem remains:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{determine the actual coefficient point of complete TECT}
}
\end{equation}
namely
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
}
\label{eq:Honest_coeff_point}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\end{equation}

Thus the final unresolved microscopic question is exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does complete TECT realize Branch A or Branch B?}
}
\label{eq:Honest_main_question}
\end{equation}

Accordingly, the honest final status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The reduced Dirac-type PDE form is proved.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The explicit strongest currently constructed microscopic realization is Branch B.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The complete microscopic theory is not yet fully closed, because the actual full-action coefficient extraction is still open.}
}
\end{equation}

So the roadmap-level conceptual problem is finished, but the final microscopic realization problem is not.
The theory is therefore in a strong conditional-closure stage rather than a final unconditional-complete stage.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual branch decision for the minimal complete TECT ansatz}

\section{Problem}

We now decide the longitudinal branch for the minimal complete lowest-order TECT ansatz.
The question is whether the actual local transport kernel contains a constant-leading longitudinal term
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}+O(\theta^2),
\]
or only the primitive commutator-square channel.

Equivalently, we must decide whether
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\ \lambda_c\neq 0.
\]

\section{Minimal complete microscopic source}

Take the lowest-order complete realization already constructed:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a
+\text{extra transverse }E/O\text{ slots}.
\label{eq:BD_Leff}
\end{equation}

For the longitudinal branch decision, only the \(\sigma_3\)-type normal component matters.
The transverse \(E/O\) slots do not contribute to \(n^\mu\sigma_3\), so they can be ignored in the longitudinal audit.

Thus the relevant microscopic currents are
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
=
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2\,A_a(\theta)\,\theta',
\label{eq:BD_J}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:BD_K}
\end{equation}

Here
\begin{equation}
m_a(\theta)=z_B^\dagger T_a z_B,
\qquad
k_a(\theta)=\Tr\!\Big[T_a(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)\Big],
\qquad
A_a(\theta)=e_1^\dagger T_a z_B+z_B^\dagger T_a e_1.
\label{eq:BD_defs}
\end{equation}

\section{Concrete generator choice}

Choose the embedded \(SU(2)_{(13)}\) generators
\begin{equation}
T_1=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&1\\
0&0&0\\
1&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T_2=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&-i\\
0&0&0\\
i&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T_3=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&0&0\\
0&0&-1
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:BD_T}
\end{equation}
and the real defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:BD_z}
\end{equation}

Then direct evaluation gives
\begin{equation}
m_1=\frac12\sin 2\theta,
\qquad
m_2=0,
\qquad
m_3=\frac12\cos 2\theta,
\label{eq:BD_m}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
k_1=\cos 2\theta,
\qquad
k_2=0,
\qquad
k_3=-\sin 2\theta,
\label{eq:BD_k}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
A_1=\cos 2\theta,
\qquad
A_2=0,
\qquad
A_3=-\sin 2\theta,
\qquad
A_a=k_a.
\label{eq:BD_A}
\end{equation}

\section{The would-be Branch A term}

Substituting \eqref{eq:BD_J} and \eqref{eq:BD_K} into \eqref{eq:BD_Leff}, the \(\theta'\)-order term is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L^{(1)}_{\parallel,\text{cand}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\phi_0\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)\,
\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:BD_candA}
\end{equation}

If this contraction were nonzero and projected to \(n^\mu\sigma_3\), it would generate a constant-leading
longitudinal coefficient \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\).

But using \eqref{eq:BD_m} and \eqref{eq:BD_k},
\begin{align}
m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)
&=
m_1k_1+m_2k_2+m_3k_3
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac12\sin 2\theta\cos 2\theta
+
0
+
\frac12\cos 2\theta(-\sin 2\theta)
\nonumber\\
&=0.
\label{eq:BD_mk_zero}
\end{align}

Therefore the entire \(\theta'\)-order longitudinal candidate vanishes identically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L^{(1)}_{\parallel,\text{cand}}=0.
}
\label{eq:BD_Avanish}
\end{equation}

Hence the minimal complete ansatz generates no Branch A term.
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:BD_Lambda0_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{The surviving primitive longitudinal term}

Now consider the higher-order normal term coming from the \(\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2A_a\theta'\) part of \(J_i^a\):
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L^{(\mathrm{prim})}_{\parallel}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\phi_0^2\,
\theta'(\xi)^2\,
A_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)\,
\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:BD_prim}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:BD_A} and \eqref{eq:BD_k},
\begin{align}
A_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)
&=
A_1k_1+A_2k_2+A_3k_3
\nonumber\\
&=
\cos^2 2\theta+0+(-\sin 2\theta)(-\sin 2\theta)
\nonumber\\
&=1.
\label{eq:BD_Ak_one}
\end{align}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L^{(\mathrm{prim})}_{\parallel}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\phi_0^2\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\mathcal O[\psi].
}
\label{eq:BD_prim_nonzero}
\end{equation}

After tangent projection, this is exactly the commutator-square channel
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\label{eq:BD_commsq}
\end{equation}
hence the longitudinal transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:BD_Vpar}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\neq 0
\qquad
(\alpha\beta\neq 0).
}
\label{eq:BD_lambdac}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:BD_lambda}
\end{equation}

\section{Branch decision}

Equations \eqref{eq:BD_Lambda0_zero} and \eqref{eq:BD_lambdac} give the exact branch decision:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:BD_decision}
\end{equation}

Therefore the minimal complete lowest-order TECT ansatz lies \emph{exactly} on Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{minimal complete LO TECT} \in \text{Branch B}.
}
\label{eq:BD_branchB}
\end{equation}

\section{Final reduced PDE for the solved branch}

Combining the already constructed transverse completion \((\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0)\),
the reduced principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{LO}}(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:BD_finalPDE}
\end{equation}

Its nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta,\cos}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:BD_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{What remains open}

This solves the branch ambiguity for the \emph{minimal complete lowest-order ansatz}.
What remains open is only whether the true final complete TECT action contains additional microscopic
operators that generate
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\]
thereby moving the theory from Branch B to Branch A.

So the branch problem is solved at the level of the present complete lowest-order realization,
but not yet for the unknown ultimate full action.

\section{Final Summary}

For the concrete \(SU(2)_{(13)}\) generator choice and real defect representative,
the \(\theta'\)-order longitudinal contraction vanishes exactly:
\[
m_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)=0.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\]

The primitive higher-order contraction survives exactly:
\[
A_a(\theta)k_a(\theta)=1.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c=-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\neq 0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

Therefore the minimal complete lowest-order TECT realization lies exactly on Branch B:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\qquad \lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\]

Including the already constructed transverse completion, the solved reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{LO}}(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

So the branch ambiguity is solved for the present minimal complete lowest-order ansatz:
it is Branch B.
The only remaining open question is whether the ultimate full complete TECT action contains extra
operators that can generate a nonzero constant-leading longitudinal coefficient \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\),
thereby realizing Branch A instead.

What is not solved yet is whether the ultimate full complete TECT action contains additional microscopic operators generating
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\]
which would move the theory from Branch B to Branch A.

\section{Final Summary}

At the present stage, the actually solved final PDE is the reduced Branch B PDE of the minimal complete lowest-order TECT realization:

\[
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{LO}}(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+

\section{Removal of the main weakness by a weaker but sufficient microscopic criterion}

\section{Main weakness}

The main remaining weakness is the absence of a direct proof that the true complete TECT action
realizes a nontrivial Class II carrier sector in the physically relevant defect background.

At the current document level, this is the exact remaining open issue:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the true complete microscopic TECT linearization contain a shell-relevant }(i,a)\text{-carrier sector?}
}
\label{eq:weakness_main}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{Key observation}

This weakness can be removed as a \emph{logical bottleneck} by replacing the overly strong requirement

\[
\text{``prove the full complete Class II realization first''}
\]

with the weaker but already sufficient requirement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{show that the actual microscopic transport space }V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ contains one longitudinal seed direction and one transverse seed direction.}
}
\label{eq:weakness_weaker_requirement}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{Canonical seed basis}

Inside the minimal Class II seed family, the shell-adapted tensor basis is
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:weakness_seed_basis}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the seed coordinates
\[
(c_\parallel,c_I,c_J),
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\label{eq:weakness_gcgego}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

Therefore the canonical explicit seed directions are:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,\quad c_I=c_J=0
\Longrightarrow
g_c\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:weakness_long_seed}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel=0,\quad c_I\neq 0,\quad c_J=0
\Longrightarrow
g_E\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:weakness_even_seed}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel=0,\quad c_I=0,\quad c_J\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
g_O\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:weakness_odd_seed}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{Practical replacement theorem}

Let \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) be the true symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space extracted from the
complete TECT Hessian around the relevant defect background.

Assume that:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\,N_\parallel\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ such that }
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_\parallel\rangle\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:weakness_assump_long}
\end{equation}

and

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\,N_\perp\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ such that }
\langle T^{(\perp)},N_\perp\rangle\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:weakness_assump_trans}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,
\qquad
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\perp)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:weakness_projection_condition}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Then the witness channels survive generically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:weakness_generic_survival}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:weakness_dirac_survival}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\section{What this removes}

This does \emph{not} prove the entire final complete TECT action in one stroke.
What it removes is the strongest remaining logical weakness:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{we no longer need a full microscopic proof of all Class II completion terms before concluding local Dirac nondegeneracy.}
}
\label{eq:weakness_removed_logical}
\end{equation}

Instead, it is sufficient to prove the much weaker finite statement:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the complete microscopic transport space contains one admissible longitudinal seed and one admissible transverse seed.}
}
\label{eq:weakness_removed_finite}
\end{equation}

Thus the open problem is compressed from
\[
\text{``derive the entire full completion first''}
\]
to
\[
\text{``perform a finite seed-embedding check in the complete Hessian.''}
\]

\section{Final practical consequence}

Therefore the main weakness is removed in the following precise sense:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the unresolved microscopic completion is no longer a conceptual obstruction; it is only a finite transport-space embedding check.}
}
\label{eq:weakness_removed_final}
\end{equation}

So the actual deliverable is now:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{extract }V_{\mathrm{micro}}\text{ from the full Hessian and verify that it contains one longitudinal seed and one transverse seed from }V_{\mathrm{seed}}.
}
\label{eq:weakness_deliverable}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The main weakness was:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no direct proof yet that the full complete TECT action realizes a nontrivial Class II carrier sector.}
}
\]

This weakness can be removed as a logical bottleneck by replacing the overly strong requirement
of proving the full Class II completion first with the weaker finite sufficient condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic transport space }V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ contains one longitudinal seed and one transverse seed.}
}
\]

Inside the canonical Class II seed family,
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J,
\]
so explicit seed directions already exist:
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0\Rightarrow g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
c_I\neq 0\Rightarrow g_E\neq 0,
\qquad
c_J\neq 0\Rightarrow g_O\neq 0.
\]

Therefore it is sufficient to verify in the complete Hessian that
\[
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,
\qquad
P_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}T^{(\perp)}\neq 0.
\]

Once this finite seed-embedding check holds, one obtains
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0),
\]
hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

So the main weakness is removed in the precise sense that the remaining microscopic task is no longer
a full completion proof, but only a finite seed-embedding audit in the true complete TECT Hessian.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Finite seed-embedding test from the complete microscopic Hessian}

\section{Complete Hessian and first-order transport block}

Let the full complete TECT linearization around the relevant defect background be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\mathbb H_B
-
i\,\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\,\partial_{y^\mu}
+
O(\partial_y^2).
}
\label{eq:Proj_Hfull}
\end{equation}

The shell-relevant first-order transport kernel is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_1=-i\,V^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi):=\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\big|_{Q_B\text{-tangent sector}}.
}
\label{eq:Proj_L1}
\end{equation}

\section{Low-mode projection}

Choose the opposite-valley low-mode basis
\[
\{u_a^+(\xi),u_a^-(\xi)\}_{a=1,2}
\]
on the tangent bundle \(Q_B(\xi)\). The reduced \(2\times 2\) transport matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,\,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
}
\label{eq:Proj_Mmu}
\end{equation}

These are the only objects needed to read the actual coefficient point.

\section{Canonical seed basis in the ambient tensor space}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient enriched tensor space. Define the shell-seed basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\parallel,\qquad B_I,\qquad B_J,
}
\label{eq:Proj_seed_basis}
\end{equation}
corresponding to
\[
B_\parallel\leftrightarrow \hat n_i\delta^{a3},
\qquad
B_I\leftrightarrow e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2},
\qquad
B_J\leftrightarrow -e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}.
\]

Then any shell-relevant microscopic transport tensor can be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
c_\parallel B_\parallel
+
c_I B_I
+
c_J B_J
+
N_\perp^{\mathrm{null}},
}
\label{eq:Proj_Nmic}
\end{equation}
where \(N_\perp^{\mathrm{null}}\) lies in the kernel of the shell witness map.

\section{Projection formulas for the coefficients}

Introduce the canonical witness covectors
\[
T^{(\parallel)},\qquad T^{(I)},\qquad T^{(J)}.
\]
By orthogonality in the normalized shell frame,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle T^{(\parallel)},B_I\rangle=
\langle T^{(\parallel)},B_J\rangle=0,
}
\label{eq:Proj_orth1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle T^{(I)},B_\parallel\rangle=
\langle T^{(I)},B_J\rangle=0,
}
\label{eq:Proj_orth2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle T^{(J)},B_\parallel\rangle=
\langle T^{(J)},B_I\rangle=0,
}
\label{eq:Proj_orth3}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\parallel:=\langle T^{(\parallel)},B_\parallel\rangle\neq 0,
\quad
\mu_I:=\langle T^{(I)},B_I\rangle\neq 0,
\quad
\mu_J:=\langle T^{(J)},B_J\rangle\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Proj_mu_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Therefore the coefficients are extracted directly by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\frac{\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_{\mathrm{mic}}\rangle}{\mu_\parallel},
\qquad
c_I
=
\frac{\langle T^{(I)},N_{\mathrm{mic}}\rangle}{\mu_I},
\qquad
c_J
=
\frac{\langle T^{(J)},N_{\mathrm{mic}}\rangle}{\mu_J}.
}
\label{eq:Proj_coeff_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{Equivalent matrix formulas from \texorpdfstring{$M^\mu$}{Mmu}}

Equivalently, define the reduced coefficient functionals by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu M^\mu\bigr],
}
\label{eq:Proj_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl[\sigma_1\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu+\sigma_2\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu\bigr],
}
\label{eq:Proj_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl[\sigma_2\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu-\sigma_1\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu\bigr].
}
\label{eq:Proj_beta}
\end{equation}

In the canonical seed normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\mu_\parallel c_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=\mu_I c_I,
\qquad
\beta=\mu_J c_J.
}
\label{eq:Proj_lambdageneric}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:Proj_long_equiv}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_I,c_J)\neq(0,0)
\Longleftrightarrow
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:Proj_trans_equiv}
\end{equation}

\section{Finite embedding test}

The entire complete microscopic audit is therefore reduced to the following finite projection test:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{seed}}}N_{\mathrm{mic}}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Proj_embedding_basic}
\end{equation}

More explicitly, the actual carrier survives iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Proj_embedding_full}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in witness form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_{\mathrm{mic}}\rangle\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(
\langle T^{(I)},N_{\mathrm{mic}}\rangle,\,
\langle T^{(J)},N_{\mathrm{mic}}\rangle
\bigr)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Proj_witness_test}
\end{equation}

\section{Algorithmic form}

Thus the complete microscopic seed-embedding check is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute the complete Hessian \(\mathbb H_{\mathrm{comp}}\) and extract \(\mathbb H_1^\mu\).
\item Restrict \(\mathbb H_1^\mu\) to the tangent low-mode sector to get \(V^\mu(\xi)\).
\item Compute
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]
\item Evaluate \eqref{eq:Proj_lambda}--\eqref{eq:Proj_beta}.
\item Read
\[
c_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel/\mu_\parallel,\qquad
c_I=\alpha/\mu_I,\qquad
c_J=\beta/\mu_J.
\]
\item Conclude that the complete microscopic transport space contains the required seed directions iff
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{Sharp final form}

Therefore the remaining open microscopic problem is no longer vague.
It is exactly the finite question:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete Hessian produce a shell-projected transport tensor }N_{\mathrm{mic}}
\text{ with }
c_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0)\ ?
}
\label{eq:Proj_final_question}
\end{equation}

If yes, then the reduced PDE is automatically Dirac-nondegenerate.

\section{Final Summary}

The complete microscopic seed-embedding problem reduces to a finite projection formula.

From the full complete TECT Hessian
\[
\mathbb H_{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\mathbb H_B
-
i\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
O(\partial_y^2),
\]
extract the shell transport kernel
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\big|_{Q_B\text{-tangent sector}}.
\]

Project to the opposite-valley low modes:
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]

Then define
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3\,n_\mu M^\mu],
\qquad
\alpha
=
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_1\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu+\sigma_2\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu],
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_2\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu-\sigma_1\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu].
\]

In the canonical seed normalization,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\mu_\parallel c_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=\mu_I c_I,
\qquad
\beta=\mu_J c_J,
\]
with
\[
\mu_\parallel,\mu_I,\mu_J\neq 0.
\]

Therefore the complete microscopic carrier survives iff
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Equivalently, the remaining microscopic question is exactly:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the complete Hessian produce a shell-projected tensor with nonzero longitudinal seed and nonzero transverse seed?}
}
\]

If yes, then the reduced PDE is automatically Dirac-nondegenerate.

\section{One-shot coefficient extraction from the complete Hessian}

\section{Complete first-order operator}

Start from the complete microscopic first-order operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\mathbb H_B
-
i\,\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
O(\partial_y^2).
}
\label{eq:OneShot_H}
\end{equation}

Restrict to the tangent defect sector and define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi):=\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\big|_{Q_B\text{-tangent}}.
}
\label{eq:OneShot_V}
\end{equation}

Choose the opposite-valley low-mode basis
\[
\{u_1^+,u_2^+,u_1^-,u_2^-\},
\]
and define the reduced transport matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle,
\qquad a,b=1,2.
}
\label{eq:OneShot_M}
\end{equation}

\section{Pauli decomposition of the reduced transport}

For each worldvolume direction \(\mu\), decompose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu
=
m_0^\mu \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1^\mu \sigma_1
+
m_2^\mu \sigma_2
+
m_3^\mu \sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:OneShot_Pauli}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_A^\mu=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_A M^\mu),
\qquad
A=0,1,2,3,
\quad
\sigma_0:=\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:OneShot_mA}
\end{equation}

The scalar component \(m_0^\mu\) is irrelevant for the Dirac witness.
Only \(m_1^\mu,m_2^\mu,m_3^\mu\) matter.

\section{Direct extraction of the three seed coordinates}

Let
\[
n_\mu,\qquad e_{1\mu},\qquad e_{2\mu}
\]
be the shell-adapted orthonormal frame.
Define the three reduced coefficients by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_3\,n_\mu M^\mu\bigr)
=
n_\mu m_3^\mu,
}
\label{eq:OneShot_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_1\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu+\sigma_2\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu\bigr)
=
e_{1\mu}m_1^\mu+e_{2\mu}m_2^\mu,
}
\label{eq:OneShot_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_2\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu-\sigma_1\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu\bigr)
=
e_{1\mu}m_2^\mu-e_{2\mu}m_1^\mu.
}
\label{eq:OneShot_beta}
\end{equation}

These are the exact one-shot coefficient functionals.

\section{Canonical seed normalization}

Let the shell-seed basis be
\[
B_\parallel,\qquad B_I,\qquad B_J,
\]
with canonical witness overlaps
\[
\mu_\parallel=\langle T^{(\parallel)},B_\parallel\rangle\neq 0,
\qquad
\mu_I=\langle T^{(I)},B_I\rangle\neq 0,
\qquad
\mu_J=\langle T^{(J)},B_J\rangle\neq 0.
\]
Then the seed coordinates are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\mu_\parallel},
\qquad
c_I=\frac{\alpha}{\mu_I},
\qquad
c_J=\frac{\beta}{\mu_J}.
}
\label{eq:OneShot_ccoords}
\end{equation}

Therefore the final microscopic embedding test is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:OneShot_embedding}
\end{equation}

\section{Equivalent branch-sensitive interpretation}

The longitudinal branch is determined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(0)\bigr].
}
\label{eq:OneShot_Lambda0}
\end{equation}

Hence:

\paragraph{Branch A.}
If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta \Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}+O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
\]

\paragraph{Branch B.}
If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
then one computes the primitive coefficient
\[
\lambda_c
\]
from the projection onto the seed
\[
\theta'(\xi)S_\xi n^\mu,
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
Then
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

\section{Solved lowest-order Branch B realization}

For the already solved minimal complete lowest-order realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:OneShot_Vsolved}
\end{equation}

Projecting with \eqref{eq:OneShot_M} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:OneShot_solvedcoeffs}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_{\theta,\cos}:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:OneShot_overlaps}
\end{equation}

Hence for the solved lowest-order realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2\mu_\parallel}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
c_I
=
\frac{I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E}{\mu_I},
\qquad
c_J
=
\frac{I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O}{\mu_J}.
}
\label{eq:OneShot_solvedc}
\end{equation}

Thus the solved lowest-order realization is Dirac-nondegenerate iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta,\cos}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:OneShot_solvednondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{Final microscopic deliverable}

Therefore the actual remaining microscopic task is completely explicit:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }M^\mu_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
\text{ from the complete Hessian, then read }
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\text{ from \eqref{eq:OneShot_lambda}--\eqref{eq:OneShot_beta}.}
}
\label{eq:OneShot_deliverable}
\end{equation}

No further structural reduction is needed.

\section{Final Summary}

The complete microscopic seed-embedding audit is now a direct projection formula.

From the full complete Hessian
\[
\mathbb H_{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\mathbb H_B-i\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}+O(\partial_y^2),
\]
restrict to the tangent sector:
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\big|_{Q_B\text{-tangent}}.
\]

Project to the opposite-valley low modes:
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]

Then extract
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3\,n_\mu M^\mu),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu+\sigma_2\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu),
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu-\sigma_1\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu).
\]

In canonical seed normalization,
\[
c_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel/\mu_\parallel,
\qquad
c_I=\alpha/\mu_I,
\qquad
c_J=\beta/\mu_J.
\]

Therefore the final microscopic embedding test is exactly
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

For the already solved lowest-order Branch B realization,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O.
\]

So the remaining microscopic deliverable is completely explicit:
compute \(M^\mu\) from the complete Hessian and read the three coefficients directly.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Direct computation of \texorpdfstring{$M^\mu$}{Mmu} from a full tangent-compatible Hessian ansatz}

\section{Goal}

We now write the most general lowest-order tangent-compatible first-order Hessian block
for the complete TECT action and project it directly to the low opposite-valley sector.

The purpose is to obtain the coefficient extraction
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
in one shot from the complete microscopic Hessian.

\section{Tangent bundle basis}

On the defect background, take the tangent bundle basis
\[
Q_B(\xi)=\mathrm{span}\{e_1(\xi),e_2\},
\]
with
\[
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Define the tangent Pauli operators by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_1=|e_1\rangle\langle e_2|+|e_2\rangle\langle e_1|,
\qquad
\Sigma_2=-i|e_1\rangle\langle e_2|+i|e_2\rangle\langle e_1|,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|-|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_Sigma}
\end{equation}

Also let
\[
\Pi_Q=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|+|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
\]

\section{Most general shell-compatible first-order tangent block}

The complete first-order microscopic operator restricted to the tangent sector must have the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
a_0(\xi)\,n^\mu\Pi_Q
+
a_3(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
b_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
b_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_Vgeneral}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(a_0(\xi)\) is scalar and irrelevant to the reduced Dirac witness;
\item \(a_3(\xi)\) is the longitudinal traceless coefficient;
\item \(b_E(\xi)\) is the transverse-even coefficient;
\item \(b_O(\xi)\) is the transverse-odd coefficient;
\item \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}\) is any tangent operator orthogonal to the shell witness map.
\end{itemize}

Thus all load-bearing information is contained in
\[
a_3(\xi),\qquad b_E(\xi),\qquad b_O(\xi).
\]

\section{Branch-sensitive parametrization}

To make the longitudinal branch structure explicit, write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_a3}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_E(\xi)
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
+
b_E^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_bE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O(\xi)
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
+
b_O^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_bO}
\end{equation}

This separates:

\begin{itemize}
\item Branch A candidate: \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,\theta'(\xi)n^\mu\Sigma_3\);
\item Branch B primitive term: \(\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3n^\mu\Sigma_3\);
\item explicit transverse completion: \(\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)\,[\widetilde\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+\widetilde\Lambda_OJ^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a]\).
\end{itemize}

\section{Low opposite-valley basis}

Choose the low-mode basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_1^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\qquad
u_2^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_2.
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_lowmodes}
\end{equation}

Assume the standard normalization
\[
\int d\xi\,|f_\pm(\xi)|^2=1,
\qquad
\langle u_a^\pm,u_b^\pm\rangle=\delta_{ab},
\qquad
\langle u_a^+,u_b^-\rangle=0.
\]

Define the overlap integrals
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_0:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi),
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_I0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_I3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_c:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_Ic}
\end{equation}

\section{Matrix-element computation}

The reduced transport matrix is
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]

Using
\[
\langle e_a,\Pi_Q e_b\rangle=\delta_{ab},
\qquad
\langle e_a,\Sigma_i e_b\rangle=(\sigma_i)_{ab},
\]
one gets immediately:
\begin{align}
M^\mu
&=
n^\mu
\left[
\left(\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,a_0(\xi)\right)\mathbf 1_2
+
\left(\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,a_3(\xi)\right)\sigma_3
\right]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\left(\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,b_E(\xi)\right)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\left(\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,b_O(\xi)\right)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
M^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}.
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_Mgeneral}
\end{align}

Therefore the load-bearing reduced matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu_{\mathrm{red}}
=
n^\mu\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3
+
\alpha\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\beta\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_Mred}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,a_3(\xi),
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,b_E(\xi),
\qquad
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,b_O(\xi).
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_alphabeta}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:HessAnsatz_a3}--\eqref{eq:HessAnsatz_bO} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_0
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
+
\delta\lambda_{\mathrm{higher}},
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_lambda_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c
+
\delta\alpha_{\mathrm{higher}},
\qquad
\beta
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c
+
\delta\beta_{\mathrm{higher}}.
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_alphabeta_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{Lowest-order solved realization}

For the already solved minimal complete lowest-order realization, one has
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}=0,
\qquad
b_E^{\mathrm{higher}}=0,
\qquad
b_O^{\mathrm{higher}}=0.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_solvedcoeffs}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu_{\mathrm{red}}
=
n^\mu\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3
+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_solvedM}
\end{equation}

\section{One-shot witness extraction}

Now apply the coefficient functionals:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3\,n_\mu M^\mu),
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_trace_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu+\sigma_2\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu),
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_trace_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2\,e_{1\mu}M^\mu-\sigma_1\,e_{2\mu}M^\mu).
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_trace_beta}
\end{equation}

These give exactly \eqref{eq:HessAnsatz_lambda_explicit}--\eqref{eq:HessAnsatz_alphabeta_explicit}.

\section{Final reduced PDE}

Therefore the reduced first-order PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_finalPDE}
\end{equation}

In the solved minimal lowest-order Branch B realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_finalPDE_solved}
\end{equation}

\section{Nondegeneracy}

The full lowest-order Dirac nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_nondeg}
\end{equation}

For the solved lowest-order realization, this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
\qquad
I_3\neq 0,
\qquad
I_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:HessAnsatz_nondeg_solved}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Given the complete first-order tangent Hessian block
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=a_0(\xi)n^\mu\Pi_Q+a_3(\xi)n^\mu\Sigma_3+b_E(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+b_O(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+\cdots,
\]
the low-mode projection
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
\]
gives
\[
M^\mu_{\mathrm{red}}
=
n^\mu\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\beta J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,a_3(\xi),
\qquad
\alpha=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,b_E(\xi),
\qquad
\beta=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,b_O(\xi).
\]

Using
\[
a_3(\xi)=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)+\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3+\cdots,
\]
\[
b_E(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_E\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)+\cdots,
\qquad
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)+\cdots,
\]
one gets
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_0+\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3+\cdots,
\qquad
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c+\cdots,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c+\cdots.
\]

For the solved minimal lowest-order realization,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
\]

Thus the solved reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

The only remaining microscopic task is to compute \(a_3,b_E,b_O\), equivalently \(M^\mu\), from the true full complete TECT Hessian.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact microscopic extraction of \texorpdfstring{$a_3(\xi),\,b_E(\xi),\,b_O(\xi)$}{a3,bE,bO} from the full complete TECT Hessian}

\section{Complete action and Hessian expansion}

Let the full complete microscopic TECT action be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{comp}}[\Phi],
\qquad
\Phi=(\Psi,P,\sigma,X).
}
\label{eq:FullH_action}
\end{equation}

Let \(\Phi_B(\xi)\) be the relevant static defect background.
Linearize around it:
\[
\Phi=\Phi_B+\delta\Phi.
\]

The quadratic fluctuation action is
\begin{equation}
\delta^2 S_{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\frac12
\int dtd^3x\;
\delta\Phi^\dagger\,
\mathbb H_{\mathrm{comp}}\,
\delta\Phi.
\label{eq:FullH_quad}
\end{equation}

Split coordinates into the defect normal coordinate \(\xi\) and worldvolume coordinates \(y^\mu\).
Then the complete Hessian admits the first-order expansion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\mathbb H_B(\xi)
-
i\,\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\,\partial_{y^\mu}
+
O(\partial_y^2).
}
\label{eq:FullH_firstorder}
\end{equation}

\section{Tangent-sector reduction}

Let
\[
Q_B(\xi)=\mathrm{span}\{e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)\}
\]
be the complex rank-two tangent bundle of the defect background, with projector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q(\xi)=|e_1(\xi)\rangle\langle e_1(\xi)|+|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
}
\label{eq:FullH_PiQ}
\end{equation}

Define the tangent Pauli basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_1=|e_1\rangle\langle e_2|+|e_2\rangle\langle e_1|,
\qquad
\Sigma_2=-i|e_1\rangle\langle e_2|+i|e_2\rangle\langle e_1|,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|-|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
}
\label{eq:FullH_Sigma}
\end{equation}

Restrict the first-order Hessian to the tangent sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi):=\Pi_Q(\xi)\,\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\,\Pi_Q(\xi).
}
\label{eq:FullH_Vmu}
\end{equation}

This is the exact microscopic transport operator relevant for the reduced Dirac problem.

\section{General tangent decomposition}

Since \(V^\mu(\xi)\) acts on a two-dimensional complex tangent space, it has the unique decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
v_0^\mu(\xi)\,\mathbf 1_2
+
v_1^\mu(\xi)\,\Sigma_1
+
v_2^\mu(\xi)\,\Sigma_2
+
v_3^\mu(\xi)\,\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:FullH_Vpauli}
\end{equation}

The scalar component \(v_0^\mu\) is irrelevant for the reduced Dirac witness.
Thus only \(v_1^\mu,v_2^\mu,v_3^\mu\) matter.

Introduce the shell-adapted worldvolume frame
\[
n^\mu,\qquad E^\mu{}_a,\qquad J^\mu{}_a,
\]
where \(n^\mu\) is the longitudinal direction and \(E^\mu{}_a,J^\mu{}_a\) are the transverse even/odd tensors.

Then the load-bearing decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
a_0(\xi)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
a_3(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
b_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
b_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:FullH_loadbearing}
\end{equation}
where \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}\) is orthogonal to the shell witness map.

\section{Direct microscopic projection formulas}

The coefficients \(a_3,b_E,b_O\) are obtained by orthogonal projection onto the corresponding tensor directions.

\subsection{Longitudinal coefficient}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:FullH_a3}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Transverse-even coefficient}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_E(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,E_\mu{}^a\,V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:FullH_bE}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Transverse-odd coefficient}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,J_\mu{}^a\,V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:FullH_bO}
\end{equation}

These are the exact one-shot microscopic extraction formulas from the complete Hessian.

\section{Branch-sensitive longitudinal split}

To decide the longitudinal branch, expand \(a_3(\xi)\) in the defect-gradient hierarchy:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\delta a_3^{(\ge 5)}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:FullH_a3_expand}
\end{equation}

Then:

\paragraph{Branch A.}
If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\]
the constant-leading longitudinal term is present.

\paragraph{Branch B.}
If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\]
the longitudinal sector survives only through the primitive \(\theta'^3\) channel.

\section{Low-mode projection}

Choose opposite-valley low modes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_1^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\qquad
u_2^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_2.
}
\label{eq:FullH_lowmodes}
\end{equation}

Define the reduced transport matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
}
\label{eq:FullH_Mmu}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:FullH_loadbearing}, the reduced matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu
=
n^\mu \lambda_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\beta\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
}
\label{eq:FullH_Mred}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,a_3(\xi),
}
\label{eq:FullH_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,b_E(\xi),
\qquad
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,b_O(\xi).
}
\label{eq:FullH_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

\section{Lowest-order solved realization as a special case}

For the already solved minimal complete lowest-order realization,
\[
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
b_E(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c,
}
\label{eq:FullH_LOcoeffs}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:FullH_I3Ic}
\end{equation}

\section{Final reduced PDE}

Therefore the reduced first-order PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:FullH_finalPDE}
\end{equation}

In the solved lowest-order Branch B realization this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:FullH_finalPDE_LO}
\end{equation}

\section{Final microscopic deliverable}

Thus the true full complete TECT microscopic problem is reduced to computing directly from \(\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu \Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q\bigr),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_E(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,E_\mu{}^a \Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q\bigr),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,J_\mu{}^a \Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

Once these are known, the coefficient point \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\) and the branch choice are fixed automatically.

\section{Final Summary}

The full complete TECT Hessian determines everything through the tangent first-order block
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q.
\]

Its load-bearing coefficients are extracted directly by
\[
a_3(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu),
\]
\[
b_E(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\,E_\mu{}^a V^\mu),
\qquad
b_O(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\,J_\mu{}^a V^\mu).
\]

Then the reduced coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,a_3(\xi),
\qquad
\alpha=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,b_E(\xi),
\qquad
\beta=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,b_O(\xi).
\]

So the complete microscopic closure problem is no longer conceptual:
it is exactly the computation of \(a_3,b_E,b_O\) from the true full complete Hessian.

For the already solved minimal lowest-order Branch B realization,
\[
a_3=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^3,
\qquad
b_E=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'\cos\theta,
\qquad
b_O=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'\cos\theta,
\]
hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
\]

Thus the solved reduced PDE is
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2))
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1))
\Bigr]\chi=0.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Term-by-term extraction of \texorpdfstring{$a_3,b_E,b_O$}{a3,bE,bO} from the complete action}

\section{Complete action split}

Write the complete action as
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{comp}}=S_\Psi+S_P+S_\sigma+S_X+S_{\mathrm{mix}},
\label{eq:TT_action_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{mix}}=S_J+S_K+S_{EO}.
\label{eq:TT_mix_split}
\end{equation}

Around the defect background \(\Phi_B=(\Psi_B,P_B,\sigma_B,X_B)\), the first-order worldvolume Hessian coefficient is additive:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_1^\mu
=
\mathbb H_{1,\Psi}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,P}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,\sigma}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,X}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,J}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,K}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,EO}^\mu.
}
\label{eq:TT_H1_split}
\end{equation}

Hence the tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu
=
\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q
=
V_\Psi^\mu+V_P^\mu+V_\sigma^\mu+V_X^\mu+V_J^\mu+V_K^\mu+V_{EO}^\mu.
}
\label{eq:TT_V_split}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3=a_3^{(\Psi)}+a_3^{(P)}+a_3^{(\sigma)}+a_3^{(X)}+a_3^{(J)}+a_3^{(K)}+a_3^{(EO)},
}
\label{eq:TT_a3_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_E=b_E^{(\Psi)}+b_E^{(P)}+b_E^{(\sigma)}+b_E^{(X)}+b_E^{(J)}+b_E^{(K)}+b_E^{(EO)},
}
\label{eq:TT_bE_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O=b_O^{(\Psi)}+b_O^{(P)}+b_O^{(\sigma)}+b_O^{(X)}+b_O^{(J)}+b_O^{(K)}+b_O^{(EO)}.
}
\label{eq:TT_bO_split}
\end{equation}

\section{Direct projection formulas}

For each sector \(S\in\{\Psi,P,\sigma,X,J,K,EO\}\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(S)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V_S^\mu(\xi)\bigr),
}
\label{eq:TT_a3_sector}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_E^{(S)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,E_\mu{}^a\,V_S^\mu(\xi)\bigr),
}
\label{eq:TT_bE_sector}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O^{(S)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,J_\mu{}^a\,V_S^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:TT_bO_sector}
\end{equation}

Thus the problem is reduced to computing \(V_S^\mu\) sector by sector.

\section{Sectors that cannot contribute at lowest order}

At lowest order:

\paragraph{Pure scalar core.}
A purely scalar shell-forming term carries no internal adjoint/tangent Pauli structure.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_E^{(\Psi,\mathrm{scalar})}=b_O^{(\Psi,\mathrm{scalar})}=0,
\qquad
a_3^{(\Psi,\mathrm{scalar})}=0.
}
\label{eq:TT_scalar_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Pure volumetric sector.}
The heavy scalar \(\sigma\) has no tangent Pauli structure by itself, so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\sigma)}=b_E^{(\sigma)}=b_O^{(\sigma)}=0
}
\label{eq:TT_sigma_zero}
\end{equation}
before mixing is included.

\paragraph{Bare heavy \(X\)-mass sector.}
The term \(\frac12M_X^2X_i^aX_i^a\) carries no worldvolume derivative and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(X)}=b_E^{(X)}=b_O^{(X)}=0.
}
\label{eq:TT_X_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus the first nontrivial lowest-order contributions must come from the refined/mixing sectors.

\section{General formula from a mixing term}

Let \(S_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(r)}\) be any mixing term.
Its quadratic Hessian contribution on the tangent sector has the generic form
\begin{equation}
\delta^2 S_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(r)}
=
\int dtd\xi d^2y\;
\eta^\dagger
\Bigl[
\mathcal A^{(r)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal B^{(r)\mu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
\Bigr]\eta
+\cdots
\label{eq:TT_generic_mix}
\end{equation}
with \(\eta\in Q_B\). Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_r^\mu(\xi)=\mathcal B^{(r)\mu}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:TT_Vr}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(r)}=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal B^{(r)\mu}),
\quad
b_E^{(r)}=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\,E_\mu{}^a\mathcal B^{(r)\mu}),
\quad
b_O^{(r)}=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\,J_\mu{}^a\mathcal B^{(r)\mu}).
}
\label{eq:TT_sector_from_B}
\end{equation}

\section{The \(J\)-sector contribution}

For
\[
J_i^a[\Psi]=(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T_a(\partial_i\Psi),
\]
the linearized defect-background contribution is
\[
J_i^a[\Psi_B+\delta\Psi]
=
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
+
\delta J_i^a[\delta\Psi].
\]
The worldvolume-derivative part of \(\delta J_i^a\) is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J_i^a\big|_{\partial_y}
=
(\partial_i\Psi_B^\dagger)T_a\,\delta\Psi_{\partial_y}
+
\delta\Psi_{\partial_y}^\dagger T_a(\partial_i\Psi_B),
}
\label{eq:TT_dJ_dy}
\end{equation}
where \(\delta\Psi_{\partial_y}\) denotes the component linear in \(\partial_{y^\mu}\eta\).

Hence the induced \(V_J^\mu\) is obtained by differentiating the quadratic form with respect to \(\partial_{y^\mu}\eta\), and then restricting to \(Q_B\).
Its contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_J^\mu
=
\Pi_Q
\frac{\partial(\delta^2 S_J)}{\partial(-i\partial_{y^\mu})}
\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:TT_VJ}
\end{equation}

At lowest order, for the real defect representative and embedded \(SU(2)_{(13)}\),
this sector contributes only to the primitive longitudinal channel and does not produce transverse \(E/O\) by itself.

\section{The \(K\)-sector contribution}

Take the minimal complete choice
\[
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T_a\partial_iP)\,(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)D_j\psi.
\]
On the defect background,
\[
\partial_iP_B=\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\,
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)D_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:TT_K_defect}
\end{equation}

Thus the direct tangent-block contribution from the \(K\)-sector has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_K^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\kappa_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\kappa_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:TT_VK}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\kappa_E(\xi)\propto k_a(\theta)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\kappa_O(\xi)\propto k_a(\theta)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
b_E^{(K)}=\kappa_E(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
b_O^{(K)}=\kappa_O(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
}
\label{eq:TT_K_contrib}
\end{equation}

\section{The extra \(E/O\) slot contribution}

For the explicit extra transverse slots,
\[
\mathcal I_E\sim X^{(E)}\Tr(S_E M_E)\,E_jD_j\psi,
\qquad
\mathcal I_O\sim X^{(O)}\Tr(S_O M_O)\,J_jD_j\psi,
\]
with
\[
\Tr(S_E M_E)=\cos\theta,
\qquad
\Tr(S_O M_O)=\cos\theta,
\]
the induced tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:TT_VEO}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(EO)}=0,
\qquad
b_E^{(EO)}=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
b_O^{(EO)}=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:TT_EO_contrib}
\end{equation}

\section{The primitive longitudinal contribution}

The primitive longitudinal channel comes from the commutator-square seed
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
For the explicit defect representative,
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
\]
Hence the primitive transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}^\mu
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:TT_Vprim}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
b_E^{(\mathrm{prim})}=0,
\qquad
b_O^{(\mathrm{prim})}=0.
}
\label{eq:TT_prim_contrib}
\end{equation}

\section{Combined lowest-order complete result}

Collecting the nonzero lowest-order pieces:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\delta a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:TT_a3_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_E(\xi)
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
+
\delta b_E^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:TT_bE_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O(\xi)
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
+
\delta b_O^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:TT_bO_final}
\end{equation}

For the solved minimal complete lowest-order realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\delta a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}=\delta b_E^{\mathrm{higher}}=\delta b_O^{\mathrm{higher}}=0.
}
\label{eq:TT_LO_special}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
b_E(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:TT_LO_result}
\end{equation}

\section{Low-mode coefficient extraction}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_0+\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3+\delta\lambda_{\mathrm{higher}},
}
\label{eq:TT_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c+\delta\alpha_{\mathrm{higher}},
\qquad
\beta
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c+\delta\beta_{\mathrm{higher}},
}
\label{eq:TT_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
with
\[
I_0=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta',
\qquad
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'\cos\theta.
\]

For the solved lowest-order realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
}
\label{eq:TT_LO_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\section{Final reduced PDE}

Thus the reduced first-order PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:TT_final_PDE}
\end{equation}

For the solved lowest-order Branch B realization this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:TT_final_PDE_LO}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The full complete TECT Hessian contributes to the reduced transport only through the tangent first-order block
\[
V^\mu=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q.
\]

Its three load-bearing coefficients are extracted by
\[
a_3(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu),
\qquad
b_E(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\,E_\mu{}^aV^\mu),
\qquad
b_O(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\,J_\mu{}^aV^\mu).
\]

At lowest order,
\[
a_3(\xi)=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)+\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3+\cdots,
\]
\[
b_E(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)+\cdots,
\qquad
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)+\cdots.
\]

For the solved minimal complete lowest-order realization,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
a_3=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^3,
\qquad
b_E=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'\cos\theta,
\qquad
b_O=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'\cos\theta.
\]

Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c,
\]
and the solved reduced PDE is
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
\]

So the only remaining microscopic task is to compute the true full-action corrections
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},
\qquad
\delta a_3^{\mathrm{higher}},
\qquad
\delta b_E^{\mathrm{higher}},
\qquad
\delta b_O^{\mathrm{higher}}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{A no-go theorem for Branch A and the necessary microscopic condition to evade it}

\section{Goal}

We now sharpen the remaining microscopic problem.

The unresolved longitudinal ambiguity was
\[
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\delta a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
\]
The question is whether the full complete TECT action can generate a nonzero constant-leading coefficient
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0.
\]

We now prove a broad no-go statement:
for a large class of real, local, tangent-isotropic complete actions built on the real \(CP^2\) defect representative,
the coefficient \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\) vanishes identically.
Therefore Branch B is forced unless the full action contains an additional microscopic operator of a specific type.

\section{Tangent geometric data}

On the explicit real defect representative,
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\]
with tangent basis
\[
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Define
\[
\Pi_Q=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|+|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|-|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
\]

The basic tangent geometric object is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
}
\label{eq:NoGo_Txi}
\end{equation}

A direct computation gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
}
\label{eq:NoGo_Tlinear_zero}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:NoGo_Tsquare}
\end{equation}

Thus the first nontrivial traceless longitudinal tangent tensor appears only at quadratic order in \(\mathcal T_\xi\), i.e. at order \(\theta'^2\).

\section{Consequence for the tangent first-order Hessian}

Let the complete first-order tangent Hessian block be
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q.
\]
Its longitudinal traceless coefficient is
\[
a_3(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
\]

Suppose the full complete action is built from local real invariants of the fields
\[
(\Psi,P,\sigma,X)
\]
and their derivatives, subject to the following two conditions:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the action contains no microscopic tangent operator whose tangent reduction is linear in \(\mathcal T_\xi\) and already proportional to \(\Sigma_3\);
\item the action is tangent-isotropic in the sense that the two tangent directions are not explicitly distinguished before the defect background is inserted.
\end{enumerate}

Then every longitudinal traceless tangent contribution must be generated from even powers of the fundamental off-diagonal tangent operator \(\mathcal T_\xi\).

By \eqref{eq:NoGo_Tlinear_zero} and \eqref{eq:NoGo_Tsquare}, the first such contribution is necessarily
\[
a_3(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)^3,
\]
not \(\theta'(\xi)\).

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{If the complete action contains no linear tangent } \Sigma_3\text{-carrier, then }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:NoGo_main}
\end{equation}

This proves the broad no-go theorem for Branch A.

\section{Proof in operator form}

Any longitudinal traceless contribution to \(V^\mu\) must have the form
\[
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)=n^\mu\,\mathcal V_\parallel(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal V_\parallel(\xi)\in \mathrm{span}\{\Sigma_3\}.
\]

Under the assumptions above, \(\mathcal V_\parallel\) can only be built from scalar functions of \(\theta\)
times tangent operators generated by \(\mathcal T_\xi\).
Since
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
the linear term vanishes.
The first nonzero traceless tangent term is
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'^2\Sigma_3.
\]
To turn this into a worldvolume first-order transport kernel one must multiply by one further odd normal factor,
namely the prefactor \(\theta'(\xi)\) coming from the first-order defect transport structure
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]
Hence the first nonzero longitudinal traceless term is necessarily
\[
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)\sim \theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]

Therefore no \(\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3\) term can occur, and
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
\]

\section{Necessary condition for Branch A}

The no-go theorem shows that Branch A can appear only if the complete action contains an additional microscopic operator whose tangent reduction bypasses the vanishing
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0.
\]

Equivalently, Branch A requires at least one new microscopic invariant whose contribution to the first-order tangent Hessian satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V_{\mathrm{new}}^\mu(\xi)\bigr)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
O(\theta'^3).
}
\label{eq:NoGo_BranchA_needed}
\end{equation}

Thus a necessary condition for Branch A is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\ \mathcal O_{\mathrm{new}}
\text{ in the full complete action such that }
\Pi_Q\,\delta^2\mathcal O_{\mathrm{new}}\,\Pi_Q
\text{ contains a longitudinal traceless tangent term linear in }\theta'(\xi).
}
\label{eq:NoGo_newop_needed}
\end{equation}

Without such an operator, Branch A is impossible.

\section{Solved status of the present minimal complete lowest-order realization}

The present minimal complete lowest-order realization contains:

\begin{itemize}
\item the primitive commutator-square longitudinal channel;
\item the explicit transverse even/odd completions;
\item no independent linear longitudinal \(\Sigma_3\)-carrier.
\end{itemize}

Therefore it falls under the no-go theorem above, and one concludes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:NoGo_LO_branchB}
\end{equation}

Hence the solved lowest-order complete realization is necessarily on Branch B.

\section{Final reduced PDE under the no-go theorem}

Under the no-go theorem assumptions, the reduced first-order PDE is forced to be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:NoGo_finalPDE}
\end{equation}

\section{Sharp conclusion}

So the remaining microscopic task is now even sharper than before.

One no longer merely asks:
\[
\text{``Does the full complete action give Branch A or Branch B?''}
\]

Instead one asks:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the full complete TECT action contain an explicit linear longitudinal tangent carrier that violates the no-go theorem assumptions?}
}
\label{eq:NoGo_sharp_question}
\end{equation}

If the answer is no, then Branch B is forced for the full theory as well.
If the answer is yes, then Branch A becomes possible and must be checked explicitly.

\section{Final Summary}

For the real \(CP^2\) defect representative, the basic tangent operator satisfies
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
while
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
\]

Therefore, for any complete local real action that does not contain an additional linear longitudinal
tangent carrier, the first nonzero longitudinal traceless transport term is necessarily
\[
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)\sim \theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\]
for this entire class of actions.

So Branch A is impossible unless the full complete TECT action contains an extra microscopic operator
whose tangent Hessian produces a term
\[
\Pi_Q\delta^2\mathcal O_{\mathrm{new}}\Pi_Q
\supset
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]

Without such an operator, Branch B is forced.

Since the present minimal complete lowest-order realization contains no such linear longitudinal carrier,
it is necessarily on Branch B:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\qquad \lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\]

Thus the solved reduced PDE remains
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
\]

So the remaining microscopic question is now:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the ultimate full complete TECT action contain a linear longitudinal tangent carrier beyond the present lowest-order realization?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Classification of possible linear longitudinal tangent carriers}

\section{Problem}

We seek all possible local microscopic operators that could generate a longitudinal tangent contribution
of the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{new}}(\xi)
\supset
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Classify_goal}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, we want to classify all possible local invariants whose tangent Hessian contribution contains
a term linear in the defect gradient and traceless in the tangent \(2\times 2\) sector.

\section{Algebra generated by \texorpdfstring{$P$}{P} and \texorpdfstring{$\partial_\xi P$}{dP}}

Let
\[
P=P_B(\xi)=z_Bz_B^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P,\partial_\xi P].
\]
For the real defect representative,
\[
z_B=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta\\
0\\
\sin\theta
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1.
\]

Inside the tangent bundle \(Q_B\), the basic identities are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
}
\label{eq:Classify_T1}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'^2\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Classify_T2}
\end{equation}

Hence the local algebra generated purely by \(P\) and one power of \(\partial_\xi P\) has no nonzero tangent-traceless element.
The first tangent-traceless element appears only at quadratic order in \(\partial_\xi P\).

\section{General local operator ansatz at linear derivative order}

Consider any local microscopic invariant density \(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{lin}}\) which is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item local in the fields,
\item linear in the normal derivative \(\partial_\xi\),
\item built from the complete field set \((\Psi,P,\sigma,X)\),
\item tangent-isotropic before inserting the defect background.
\end{enumerate}

Its tangent Hessian contribution must have the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{lin}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\,\mathcal A_Q(\xi),
}
\label{eq:Classify_Vlin}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal A_Q(\xi)\) is a tangent endomorphism.

The question is whether \(\mathcal A_Q\) can contain a nonzero traceless part proportional to \(\Sigma_3\).

\section{No-go for isotropic local operators}

Assume \(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{lin}}\) is built only from:
\[
P,\qquad \partial_\xi P,\qquad \Psi^\dagger\Psi,\qquad \sigma,\qquad
\text{and isotropic scalar contractions.}
\]
Then after restriction to the tangent bundle, \(\mathcal A_Q\) is generated by the tangent reductions of:
\[
\Pi_Q,\qquad
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q,\qquad
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q,\qquad\ldots
\]

At linear derivative order, only \(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q\) can contribute.
But by \eqref{eq:Classify_T1},
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0.
\]
Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{No isotropic local operator built only from }(P,\partial P,\Psi^\dagger\Psi,\sigma)
\text{ can generate a linear } \theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3 \text{ term.}
}
\label{eq:Classify_nogo}
\end{equation}

Thus Branch A is impossible within this entire class.

\section{Necessary ingredient for Branch A}

To obtain
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3,
\]
one needs an additional local tangent-anisotropy carrier \(H_Q\) satisfying
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_Q\in \mathrm{End}(Q_B),
\qquad
(H_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\propto \Sigma_3,
\qquad
H_Q\notin \mathrm{Alg}(P,\partial P)_{\mathrm{iso}}.
}
\label{eq:Classify_HQ}
\end{equation}

Then a linear longitudinal term may arise from an operator of the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{\mathrm{new}}
\sim
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\,H_Q.
}
\label{eq:Classify_newop}
\end{equation}

Therefore a necessary condition for Branch A is the existence of a microscopic field or composite tensor whose tangent restriction already distinguishes \(e_1\) from \(e_2\) at zeroth derivative order.

\section{Complete classification of possibilities}

At lowest local order, there are only three logically distinct ways to realize such an \(H_Q\).

\subsection{Type I: explicit tangent anisotropy field}

Introduce a new microscopic field \(Y\) whose defect-background value induces
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\,Y_B\,\Pi_Q
=
y_0\,\mathbf 1_2+y_3\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
y_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Classify_typeI}
\end{equation}

Then an invariant such as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_I
=
n_\mu\,\Tr_Q\!\bigl(Y\,\mathcal T^\mu\bigr)
}
\label{eq:Classify_OI}
\end{equation}
can generate
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]

\subsection{Type II: explicit tangent-frame selector}

Introduce a microscopic structure \(R\) that defines a preferred tangent line inside \(Q_B\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q R \Pi_Q
=
r_1\,|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|
+
r_2\,|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|,
\qquad
r_1\neq r_2.
}
\label{eq:Classify_typeII}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
\Pi_Q R \Pi_Q
=
\frac{r_1+r_2}{2}\mathbf 1_2+\frac{r_1-r_2}{2}\Sigma_3,
\]
so any linear derivative invariant coupling \(R\) to \(\partial_\xi P\) can produce a Branch A term.

\subsection{Type III: non-isotropic condensate refinement}

A refinement of the condensate sector \(\mathcal L_\Psi^{\mathrm{ref}}\) may itself induce a tangent anisotropy tensor
\[
H_Q^{(\Psi)}
\]
after background insertion, provided it does not reduce to an isotropic scalar function of \(P\) and \(\partial P\).

Then a linear transport contribution of the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\Psi,\mathrm{new}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\,H_Q^{(\Psi)}
}
\label{eq:Classify_typeIII}
\end{equation}
with
\[
(H_Q^{(\Psi)})_{\mathrm{tr}}\propto \Sigma_3
\]
would generate Branch A.

\section{Exhaustion at lowest local order}

Therefore the lowest-order microscopic classification is exhausted by:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch A is impossible unless the full action contains a tangent-anisotropy carrier of Type I, Type II, or Type III.}
}
\label{eq:Classify_exhaustion}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, Branch A requires an additional microscopic structure whose tangent restriction distinguishes \(e_1\) and \(e_2\) before the first nontrivial power of \(\partial_\xi P\) is taken.

\section{Application to the present minimal complete LO realization}

The present minimal complete lowest-order TECT realization contains:

\begin{itemize}
\item the real projector defect \(P_B\),
\item the heavy scalar \(\sigma\),
\item the heavy carrier \(X_i^a\),
\item the transverse \(E/O\) completion,
\item no explicit tangent-anisotropy carrier of Type I, Type II, or Type III.
\end{itemize}

Hence it satisfies the no-go assumptions, and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:Classify_LO_noA}
\end{equation}

So the present minimal complete LO realization is necessarily on Branch B.

\section{Final sharpened open problem}

The remaining microscopic problem is no longer vague.
It is exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the ultimate full complete TECT action contain a Type I, Type II, or Type III tangent-anisotropy carrier?}
}
\label{eq:Classify_open}
\end{equation}

If no, then the full theory is forced to remain on Branch B.
If yes, then Branch A becomes possible and must be checked explicitly by direct Hessian projection.

\section{Final Summary}

For the real \(CP^2\) defect representative,
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\qquad
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}=\frac12\theta'^2\Sigma_3.
\]

Therefore no isotropic local operator built only from
\[
(P,\partial P,\Psi^\dagger\Psi,\sigma)
\]
can produce a linear longitudinal tangent term
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
\]

Hence Branch A is impossible unless the full complete action contains an additional tangent-anisotropy carrier \(H_Q\) with
\[
(H_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\propto \Sigma_3.
\]

At lowest local order, there are only three possibilities:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Type I: an explicit tangent-anisotropy field,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{Type II: an explicit tangent-frame selector,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{Type III: a non-isotropic condensate refinement.}
}
\]

This classification is exhaustive at lowest local order.

Since the present minimal complete lowest-order realization contains none of these,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
so it is necessarily on Branch B.

Therefore the remaining microscopic question is exactly:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the ultimate full complete TECT action contain a Type I, II, or III tangent-anisotropy carrier?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Type II completion and Branch A}

\section{Type II frame selector}

Introduce a microscopic frame-selector tensor \(R\) such that on the defect background
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q R \Pi_Q
=
r_1 |e_1\rangle\langle e_1|
+
r_2 |e_2\rangle\langle e_2|,
\qquad
r_1\neq r_2.
}
\label{eq:TII_R}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q R \Pi_Q
=
r_0\,\mathbf 1_2+r_3\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
r_0=\frac{r_1+r_2}{2},
\qquad
r_3=\frac{r_1-r_2}{2}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:TII_Rsplit}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal Type II invariant}

The lowest-order longitudinal Type II mixing is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{A}}^{(II)}
=
\gamma_A\,X_i^a\,n^i\,\Tr\!\bigl(T_a\,R\bigr)\,\partial_\xi\phi_0
+\mathrm{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:TII_LA}
\end{equation}

After integrating out the heavy field \(X_i^a\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(A)}
\sim
-\frac{\gamma_A\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\,
\Tr(T_aR)\,
\Tr(T_a\partial_\xi P)\,
D_\mu\psi.
}
\label{eq:TII_Leff}
\end{equation}

On the defect background,
\[
\Tr(T_a\partial_\xi P)\propto \theta'(\xi),
\]
so the induced tangent transport is linear in \(\theta'(\xi)\).

\section{Direct tangent reduction}

Projecting to the tangent sector gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_A^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\,\Pi_Q R \Pi_Q
=
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\,(r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3).
}
\label{eq:TII_VA}
\end{equation}

Therefore the longitudinal traceless coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(A)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V_A^\mu(\xi)\bigr)
=
r_3\,\theta'(\xi).
}
\label{eq:TII_a3}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=r_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:TII_Lambda0}
\end{equation}

So Type II immediately realizes Branch A.

\section{Reduced coefficient}

Projecting to the low modes,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(A)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,a_3^{(A)}(\xi)
=
r_3\,I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:TII_lambda}
\end{equation}

Therefore the Branch A reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{(A)}(p)
=
r_3 I_\theta\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:TII_A1}
\end{equation}

Its nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:TII_nondeg}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Internal Type II frame selector from TECT variables}

\section{Goal}

We want to realize the Type II selector
\[
