\Pi_Q R \Pi_Q=r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3,\qquad r_3\neq 0
\]
using only internal TECT variables, without introducing an external ad hoc field.

\section{Tangent-bundle data}

On the real defect background,
\[
z_B=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta\\
0\\
\sin\theta
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta\\
0\\
\cos\theta
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
\Pi_Q=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|+|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|-|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
\]

So Type II means:
\[
R_Q:=\Pi_QR\Pi_Q
=
r_1|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|+r_2|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|,
\qquad r_1\neq r_2.
\]

\section{Candidate 1: projected Hessian anisotropy from the condensate sector}

Let
\[
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
:=
\Pi_Q\,
\frac{\delta^2 S_\Psi}{\delta\eta^\dagger\delta\eta}\Big|_{\Phi_B}
\,\Pi_Q
\]
be the tangent restriction of the static \(\xi\)-normal Hessian of the condensate sector.

Define its traceless tangent part
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(\Psi)}
:=
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
-
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:Rpsi_def}
\end{equation}

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(\Psi)}\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:Rpsi_nonzero}
\end{equation}
then automatically
\[
R^{(\Psi)}=r_3^{(\Psi)}\Sigma_3
\]
for some \(r_3^{(\Psi)}\neq 0\), because any traceless Hermitian \(2\times2\) operator on \(Q_B\) is a linear combination of \(\Sigma_{1,2,3}\), and the longitudinal Type II selector keeps only the \(\Sigma_3\) component.

Thus a non-isotropic condensate Hessian already furnishes an internal Type II selector.

\section{Candidate 2: projected heavy-carrier anisotropy}

Let the heavy carrier sector contain a background-dependent quadratic kernel
\[
\mathcal K_{X,B}^{ij,ab}.
\]
After contraction with the shell-normal direction \(n_i n_j\) and the relevant internal channel, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(X)}
:=
\Pi_Q\,
\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}
\,\Pi_Q
-
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:RX_def}
\end{equation}

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(X)}\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:RX_nonzero}
\end{equation}
then again
\[
R^{(X)}=r_3^{(X)}\Sigma_3,\qquad r_3^{(X)}\neq 0.
\]

So an anisotropic heavy-carrier kernel also gives an internal Type II selector.

\section{Minimal internal realization}

Therefore the minimal internal Type II selector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R
=
R^{(\Psi)}+R^{(X)}.
}
\label{eq:R_internal_sum}
\end{equation}

Its tangent reduction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_QR\Pi_Q
=
r_0\Pi_Q+r_3\Sigma_3,
\qquad
r_3=r_3^{(\Psi)}+r_3^{(X)}.
}
\label{eq:R_internal_tangent}
\end{equation}

Hence the necessary and sufficient lowest-order internal condition for Type II is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3^{(\Psi)}+r_3^{(X)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:R_internal_condition}
\end{equation}

\section{Induced Branch A term}

Insert this \(R\) into the Type II longitudinal mixing
\[
\mathcal L_A^{(II)}
=
\gamma_A X_i^a n^i \Tr(T_aR)\,\partial_\xi\phi_0+\mathrm{h.c.}
\]
and integrate out \(X\). The tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_A^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\,(r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3).
}
\label{eq:R_internal_VA}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(A)}(\xi)=r_3\,\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=r_3.
}
\label{eq:R_internal_a3}
\end{equation}

So Branch A occurs iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:R_internal_branchA}
\end{equation}

\section{Resulting branch-sensitive PDE}

If \(r_3=0\), the theory stays on Branch B:
\[
A_1^{(B)}(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

If \(r_3\neq 0\), the theory is upgraded to Branch A:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{(A)}(p)
=
r_3 I_\theta\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:R_internal_A1}
\end{equation}

\section{Final microscopic test}

Thus the true full-action branch decision is reduced to the explicit internal test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\Pi_Q(R^{(\Psi)}+R^{(X)})\Pi_Q\bigr).
}
\label{eq:R_internal_test}
\end{equation}

If this trace vanishes, full TECT remains on Branch B.
If it is nonzero, full TECT lies on Branch A.

\section{Final Summary}

Type II does not require a new external field.
It can be realized internally from TECT variables as a tangent anisotropy selector
\[
\Pi_QR\Pi_Q=r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3.
\]

The two minimal internal sources are:

\[
R^{(\Psi)}
=
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
-\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)})\Pi_Q,
\]
coming from condensate-sector tangent Hessian anisotropy, and

\[
R^{(X)}
=
\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q
-\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q)\Pi_Q,
\]
coming from heavy-carrier kernel anisotropy.

The minimal internal selector is
\[
R=R^{(\Psi)}+R^{(X)}.
\]

Its branch-deciding coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
r_3
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\Pi_Q(R^{(\Psi)}+R^{(X)})\Pi_Q\bigr).
}
\]

If
\[
r_3=0,
\]
the theory remains on Branch B.

If
\[
r_3\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=r_3\neq 0,
\]
and the theory is promoted to Branch A.

So the ultimate full-action branch decision is now reduced to one explicit internal trace test for \(r_3\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual computation of the Type II branch trace \(r_3\)}

\section{Definition}

The Type II branch-deciding coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\Pi_Q(R^{(\Psi)}+R^{(X)})\Pi_Q\bigr).
}
\label{eq:r3_def}
\end{equation}

We now evaluate this for the present minimal complete lowest-order realization.

\section{Condensate-sector contribution}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
R^{(\Psi)}
=
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
-\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}\bigr)\Pi_Q,
\label{eq:r3_Rpsi}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}\) is the tangent restriction of the static normal Hessian of the condensate sector.

For the present minimal lowest-order condensate core, the tangent quadratic operator is isotropic on \(Q_B\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
=
h_\Psi(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:r3_Hpsi_iso}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{align}
R^{(\Psi)}
&=
h_\Psi(\xi)\Pi_Q
-
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(h_\Psi(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)\Pi_Q
\nonumber\\
&=
h_\Psi(\xi)\Pi_Q
-
\frac12(2h_\Psi(\xi))\Pi_Q
\nonumber\\
&=0.
\label{eq:r3_Rpsi_zero}
\end{align}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3^{(\Psi)}
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3\Pi_QR^{(\Psi)}\Pi_Q)=0.
}
\label{eq:r3_psi_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{Heavy-carrier contribution}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
R^{(X)}
=
\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q
-
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q\bigr)\Pi_Q.
\label{eq:r3_RX}
\end{equation}

In the present minimal lowest-order realization, the heavy-carrier sector is just the isotropic mass term
\[
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^aX_i^a,
\]
so its background-parallel kernel is proportional to the identity on the tangent bundle:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q
=
h_X(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:r3_HX_iso}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{align}
R^{(X)}
&=
h_X(\xi)\Pi_Q
-
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(h_X(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)\Pi_Q
\nonumber\\
&=
h_X(\xi)\Pi_Q
-
\frac12(2h_X(\xi))\Pi_Q
\nonumber\\
&=0.
\label{eq:r3_RX_zero}
\end{align}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3^{(X)}
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3\Pi_QR^{(X)}\Pi_Q)=0.
}
\label{eq:r3_X_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{Total branch trace}

Combining the two sectors,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3=r_3^{(\Psi)}+r_3^{(X)}=0.
}
\label{eq:r3_total_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=r_3=0.
}
\label{eq:r3_Lambda_zero}
\end{equation}

So the present minimal complete lowest-order realization cannot lie on Branch A.

\section{Branch decision}

Since the primitive channel was already shown to survive,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:r3_lambdac_nonzero}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\label{eq:r3_Lambda_again}
\end{equation}
the present realization lies exactly on Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{minimal complete LO TECT} \in \text{Branch B}.
}
\label{eq:r3_branchB}
\end{equation}

\section{Interpretation}

Thus the only way to obtain Branch A is to add a genuine tangent-anisotropic contribution to either

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
}
\label{eq:r3_need_Hpsi}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}.
}
\label{eq:r3_need_KX}
\end{equation}

Without such an anisotropic correction, the branch trace remains
\[
r_3=0,
\]
and Branch B is forced.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Calculation: local \(SO(2)\) invariance forces \(r_3=0\)}

\section{Setup}

Let \(Q_B(\xi)=\mathrm{span}\{e_1(\xi),e_2\}\) be the tangent two-plane on the real defect background, and let
\[
\Sigma_3=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|-|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
\]
The Type II branch-deciding coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,R_Q\bigr),
\qquad
R_Q:=\Pi_Q(R^{(\Psi)}+R^{(X)})\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:SO2_r3_def}
\end{equation}

We now compute \(r_3\) under the natural TECT assumption that the tangent low-energy action is local and \(SO(2)\)-invariant.

\section{Representation-theoretic lemma}

Let \(U(\varphi)\in SO(2)\) act on \(Q_B\) by
\[
e_1\mapsto \cos\varphi\,e_1+\sin\varphi\,e_2,
\qquad
e_2\mapsto -\sin\varphi\,e_1+\cos\varphi\,e_2.
\]
Suppose \(A\in \mathrm{End}(Q_B)\) is \(SO(2)\)-equivariant:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U(\varphi)\,A\,U(\varphi)^{-1}=A
\qquad
\forall \varphi.
}
\label{eq:SO2_equivariance}
\end{equation}
Then, on the real two-dimensional irreducible representation of \(SO(2)\),
Schur's lemma implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A=a\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:SO2_scalar}
\end{equation}

Therefore every local tangent Hessian kernel that preserves the transverse \(SO(2)\) symmetry is proportional to the identity on \(Q_B\).

\section{Condensate contribution}

Let
\[
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
:=
\Pi_Q\,
\frac{\delta^2 S_\Psi}{\delta\eta^\dagger\delta\eta}\Big|_{\Phi_B}
\,\Pi_Q.
\]
If the condensate-sector tangent action is local and \(SO(2)\)-invariant, then by \eqref{eq:SO2_scalar},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}=h_\Psi(\xi)\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:SO2_Hpsi}
\end{equation}

Hence its traceless part vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(\Psi)}
=
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
-
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)})\mathbf 1_2
=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_Rpsi_zero}
\end{equation}

So
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3^{(\Psi)}=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3R^{(\Psi)})=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_r3psi}
\end{equation}

\section{Heavy-carrier contribution}

Likewise let
\[
\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}
\]
be the shell-parallel heavy-carrier quadratic kernel restricted to \(Q_B\).
If the heavy-carrier kinetic sector is also tangent \(SO(2)\)-invariant, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q
=
h_X(\xi)\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:SO2_HX}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(X)}
=
\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q
-
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q)\mathbf 1_2
=0,
}
\label{eq:SO2_RX_zero}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3^{(X)}=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3R^{(X)})=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_r3X}
\end{equation}

\section{Total result}

Combining the two sectors,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3=r_3^{(\Psi)}+r_3^{(X)}=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_r3_total}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=r_3=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_Lambda_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence Branch A is impossible under local tangent \(SO(2)\) invariance.

\section{Consequence}

Under the natural TECT polarization-bundle condition that the tangent effective action is local and \(SO(2)\)-invariant, the only surviving longitudinal channel is the primitive one:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:SO2_branchB}
\end{equation}

So the theory is forced onto Branch B unless the full action contains an explicit term that breaks tangent \(SO(2)\) down to a frame selector on \(Q_B\).

\section{Necessary evasion condition}

To evade the result above, the full action must contain a tangent anisotropy operator \(R_Q\) with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[U(\varphi),R_Q]\neq 0
\quad\text{for some }\varphi,
}
\label{eq:SO2_break}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
R_Q=r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3,\qquad r_3\neq 0.
\]
Without such an explicit \(SO(2)\)-breaking tangent selector, one always has \(r_3=0\).

\section{Final Summary}

Assume the tangent low-energy sector of TECT is local and \(SO(2)\)-invariant on the transverse polarization bundle \(Q_B\). Then every tangent Hessian kernel on \(Q_B\) is \(SO(2)\)-equivariant, hence by irreducibility,
\[
A=a\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]

Therefore both the condensate tangent Hessian and the heavy-carrier tangent kernel are proportional to the identity:
\[
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}=h_\Psi(\xi)\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q=h_X(\xi)\mathbf 1_2.
\]

Their traceless parts vanish:
\[
R^{(\Psi)}=0,
\qquad
R^{(X)}=0.
\]

Hence the Type II branch trace is
\[
\boxed{
r_3
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3(R^{(\Psi)}+R^{(X)})\bigr)
=0.
}
\]

So
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\]

Therefore, under local tangent \(SO(2)\) invariance, Branch A is impossible and the theory is forced onto Branch B:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

To realize Branch A, the full action must contain an explicit tangent \(SO(2)\)-breaking selector \(R_Q=r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3\) with \(r_3\neq 0\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Conditional branch fixing from local \(SO(2)\) invariance}

\section{Aim}

We do not yet prove the full complete microscopic PDE unconditionally.
Instead, we prove the following stronger conditional statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{If the full tangent low-energy sector of TECT remains local and \(SO(2)\)-invariant on }Q_B,
\text{ then Branch A is impossible and Branch B is forced.}
}
\label{eq:SO2_goal}
\end{equation}

This removes the longitudinal branch ambiguity under one concrete microscopic symmetry assumption.

\section{Tangent bundle and branch trace}

Let
\[
Q_B(\xi)=\mathrm{span}\{e_1(\xi),e_2\},
\qquad
\Sigma_3=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|-|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
\]
The branch-deciding Type II trace is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,R_Q\bigr),
\qquad
R_Q:=\Pi_Q(R^{(\Psi)}+R^{(X)})\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:SO2_branch_trace}
\end{equation}

Branch A requires
\[
r_3\neq 0,
\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=r_3.
\]
Branch B corresponds to
\[
r_3=0
\]
with surviving primitive coefficient \(\lambda_c\neq 0\).

\section{\(SO(2)\)-equivariance lemma}

Let \(U(\varphi)\in SO(2)\) act on \(Q_B\) by
\[
e_1\mapsto \cos\varphi\,e_1+\sin\varphi\,e_2,
\qquad
e_2\mapsto -\sin\varphi\,e_1+\cos\varphi\,e_2.
\]
Suppose \(A\in\mathrm{End}(Q_B)\) is \(SO(2)\)-equivariant:
\begin{equation}
U(\varphi)AU(\varphi)^{-1}=A
\qquad
\forall\varphi.
\label{eq:SO2_equiv}
\end{equation}
Since \(Q_B\) is the real irreducible \(2\)-dimensional representation of \(SO(2)\),
Schur's lemma implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A=a\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:SO2_scalar_only}
\end{equation}

Therefore no \(SO(2)\)-equivariant tangent operator can contain a traceless \(\Sigma_3\) part.

\section{Application to the condensate tangent Hessian}

Let
\[
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
:=
\Pi_Q
\frac{\delta^2 S_\Psi}{\delta\eta^\dagger\delta\eta}\Big|_{\Phi_B}
\Pi_Q.
\]
Assume the full condensate tangent sector is local and \(SO(2)\)-invariant.
Then by \eqref{eq:SO2_scalar_only},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}=h_\Psi(\xi)\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:SO2_Hpsi_scalar}
\end{equation}
Hence its traceless part vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(\Psi)}
=
\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)}
-\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\mathcal H_{\Psi,B}^{(\xi)})\mathbf 1_2
=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_Rpsi_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{Application to the heavy-carrier kernel}

Likewise let
\[
\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}
\]
be the shell-parallel heavy-carrier quadratic kernel restricted to \(Q_B\).
Assume the heavy-carrier tangent sector is also local and \(SO(2)\)-invariant.
Then again
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q
=
h_X(\xi)\mathbf 1_2,
}
\label{eq:SO2_HX_scalar}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(X)}
=
\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q
-\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Pi_Q\mathcal K_{X,B}^{\parallel}\Pi_Q)\mathbf 1_2
=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_RX_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{Branch consequence}

Combining the two sectors,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_Q=0,
\qquad
r_3=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3R_Q)=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_r3_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_Lambda0_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence Branch A is impossible under local tangent \(SO(2)\) invariance.

\section{Primitive longitudinal survival}

The primitive commutator-square channel is still available:
\[
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
\]
Therefore the longitudinal transport survives through
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:SO2_primitive_survive}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:SO2_lambda_branchB}
\end{equation}

Thus, under the \(SO(2)\)-invariance assumption,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the complete theory is forced onto Branch B.}
}
\label{eq:SO2_branchB_forced}
\end{equation}

\section{Resulting reduced PDE}

If in addition the transverse sector remains nonzero,
\[
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
\]
the reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_final_PDE}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest scope}

This does \emph{not} finish the full microscopic PDE unconditionally.
What it proves is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{full branch ambiguity disappears if the complete tangent sector preserves local \(SO(2)\).}
}
\label{eq:SO2_scope}
\end{equation}

So the remaining microscopic question is now sharpened to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the true full complete TECT Hessian preserve local tangent \(SO(2)\), or does it contain an explicit \(SO(2)\)-breaking frame selector?}
}
\label{eq:SO2_remaining}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Term-by-term \(SO(2)\) test for the full complete TECT Hessian}

\section{Goal}

We now classify the microscopic operators of the full complete TECT action according to whether they preserve
or break the local tangent \(SO(2)\) symmetry on the polarization bundle \(Q_B\).

This directly decides whether the full theory is forced onto Branch B or can realize Branch A.

\section{Tangent \(SO(2)\) structure}

Let
\[
Q_B(\xi)=\mathrm{span}\{e_1(\xi),e_2\}
\]
be the tangent two-plane on the defect background.

Any local tangent operator on \(Q_B\) can be written as
\[
A=a_0\mathbf 1_2+a_1\Sigma_1+a_2\Sigma_2+a_3\Sigma_3.
\]

Under local tangent \(SO(2)\), the pair \((e_1,e_2)\) rotates, so:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathbf 1_2\) is an \(SO(2)\)-scalar;
\item \(\Sigma_2\) is the \(SO(2)\)-invariant antisymmetric generator;
\item \((\Sigma_1,\Sigma_3)\) transform as a spin-2 traceless symmetric doublet.
\end{itemize}

Therefore a Branch A carrier requires a nonzero \(\Sigma_3\)-component, i.e. a tangent symmetric-traceless selector.

\section{Microscopic criterion}

Let the complete action be
\[
S_{\mathrm{comp}}=S_\Psi+S_P+S_\sigma+S_X+S_{\mathrm{mix}}.
\]

For each sector \(S\), let
\[
V_S^\mu=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,S}^\mu\Pi_Q
\]
be its tangent first-order Hessian block.

Then:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Sector }S\text{ preserves local tangent }SO(2)
\iff
V_S^\mu
=
u_S^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2
+
v_S^\mu\,\Sigma_2
}
\label{eq:SO2_sector_preserve}
\end{equation}

and

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Sector }S\text{ breaks local tangent }SO(2)
\iff
V_S^\mu\text{ contains a nonzero }\Sigma_1\text{ or }\Sigma_3\text{ component.}
}
\label{eq:SO2_sector_break}
\end{equation}

Since Branch A needs a longitudinal traceless term,
\[
V^\mu\supset \theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\,\Sigma_3,
\]
the only dangerous piece is the \(\Sigma_3\)-projection:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(S)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V_S^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:SO2_a3_sector}
\end{equation}

\section{Sector-by-sector classification}

\subsection{Scalar condensate core}

Any condensate-core term depending only on scalar contractions such as
\[
\Psi^\dagger\Psi,\qquad
\partial_i\Psi^\dagger\partial_i\Psi,\qquad
(\nabla^2\Psi)^\dagger(\nabla^2\Psi),\qquad
(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^2
\]
is tangent-isotropic.

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_\Psi^\mu
=
u_\Psi^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\Psi^\mu\,\Sigma_2,
\qquad
a_3^{(\Psi)}=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_scalar_core}
\end{equation}

So the ordinary locked Brazovskii condensate core cannot generate Branch A.

\subsection{Projector geometry sector}

Any projector term built only from isotropic scalar contractions of
\[
P,\qquad \partial_\mu P,\qquad \partial_\mu\partial_\nu P,\dots
\]
and without an explicit tangent-frame selector is also tangent-isotropic.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_P^\mu
=
u_P^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2
+
v_P^\mu\,\Sigma_2,
\qquad
a_3^{(P)}=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_projector_iso}
\end{equation}

So the isotropic projector geometry sector cannot generate Branch A.

\subsection{Volumetric scalar sector}

The heavy scalar \(\sigma\) carries no tangent polarization label.
Therefore any local isotropic \(\sigma\)-sector term satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_\sigma^\mu
=
u_\sigma^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
a_3^{(\sigma)}=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_sigma}
\end{equation}

So the pure volumetric sector cannot generate Branch A.

\subsection{Isotropic heavy-carrier kernel}

If the heavy carrier has only isotropic mass/kinetic terms,
\[
\frac12 M_X^2X_i^aX_i^a
\quad\text{and isotropic derivative refinements},
\]
then its tangent restriction is again scalar:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_X^\mu
=
u_X^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2
+
v_X^\mu\,\Sigma_2,
\qquad
a_3^{(X)}=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_X_iso}
\end{equation}

So isotropic \(X\)-sector refinements also cannot generate Branch A.

\subsection{Transverse \(E/O\) completion}

The explicit \(E/O\) slots generate
\[
V_{EO}^\mu
=
b_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+b_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
\]
This is exactly what produces the transverse Dirac channels, but it is not a longitudinal frame selector.

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(EO)}=0.
}
\label{eq:SO2_EO}
\end{equation}

So \(E/O\) completion does not create Branch A.

\subsection{Primitive longitudinal channel}

The primitive commutator-square channel gives
\[
V_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}^\mu
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]
Therefore it contributes to the longitudinal witness, but only at primitive order:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:SO2_primitive}
\end{equation}

This is Branch B, not Branch A.

\section{What can generate Branch A?}

By the classification above, Branch A requires a sector \(S_{\mathrm{A}}\) whose tangent Hessian block contains
\[
V_{A}^\mu
\supset
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\,\Sigma_3.
\]

Equivalently, the microscopic action must contain a local term whose tangent reduction carries a symmetric-traceless selector on \(Q_B\).

At lowest order, this means:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch A requires an explicit local tangent \(SO(2)\)-breaking term.}
}
\label{eq:SO2_need_break}
\end{equation}

Examples would be terms containing a background-dependent rank-two selector \(R_Q\) with
\[
R_Q=r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3,\qquad r_3\neq 0.
\]

\section{Total conclusion}

Therefore, if every sector in the full complete TECT action is built from local tangent-isotropic scalar contractions,
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\Psi)}=a_3^{(P)}=a_3^{(\sigma)}=a_3^{(X)}=a_3^{(EO)}=0,
}
\label{eq:SO2_all_zero}
\end{equation}
and the only surviving longitudinal term is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:SO2_only_primitive}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:SO2_branchB_final}
\end{equation}
so the full theory is forced onto Branch B.

\section{Sharp remaining microscopic test}

The only remaining full-action test is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the true complete TECT action contain any explicit local tangent \(SO(2)\)-breaking operator?}
}
\label{eq:SO2_final_test}
\end{equation}

If no, then Branch B is exact.

If yes, then compute
\[
a_3^{(A)}(\xi)=\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V_A^\mu(\xi))
\]
and decide whether \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\).

\section{Final Summary}

The term-by-term \(SO(2)\) test is:

\[
\text{sector }S\text{ preserves tangent }SO(2)
\iff
V_S^\mu=u_S^\mu\mathbf 1_2+v_S^\mu\Sigma_2,
\]
and Branch A is possible only if some sector contains a nonzero longitudinal \(\Sigma_3\) component.

For the following sectors:

\[
S_\Psi \text{ (scalar condensate core),}\quad
S_P \text{ (isotropic projector geometry),}\quad
S_\sigma \text{ (volumetric scalar),}\quad
S_X \text{ (isotropic heavy-carrier kernel),}\quad
S_{EO} \text{ (transverse completion),}
\]
one has
\[
a_3^{(S)}=0.
\]

The primitive channel contributes only
\[
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^3,
\]
which is Branch B.

Therefore, if the full complete TECT action contains only local tangent-isotropic sectors, then
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\]
so the full theory is forced onto Branch B.

Thus the only remaining microscopic question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the true complete TECT action contain any explicit local tangent \(SO(2)\)-breaking operator?}
}
\]

If no, Branch B is exact. If yes, Branch A becomes possible.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exhaustion of lowest-order local \(SO(2)\)-breaking candidates from existing TECT variables}

\section{Problem}

We now test whether an explicit local tangent \(SO(2)\)-breaking longitudinal selector can be built at lowest local order from the existing TECT variables
\[
(\Psi,\ P,\ \sigma,\ X_i^a)
\]
without introducing any new independent microscopic field.

The target is a tangent operator \(R_Q\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_Q
=
r_0\,\mathbf 1_2+r_3\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
r_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_target}
\end{equation}

If no such operator exists, then Branch A is excluded at this order.

\section{Available local building blocks}

On the real defect background, the available local objects are:

\[
P_B=z_Bz_B^\dagger,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B,
\qquad
\Psi_B=\phi_0 z_B,
\qquad
\sigma_B,
\qquad
X_{i,B}^a.
\]

At lowest local order, every candidate tangent operator must be built from algebraic combinations of:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q,\qquad
P_B,\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad
\Psi_B\Psi_B^\dagger,\qquad
\sigma_B,\qquad
X_{i,B}^aT_a.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_blocks}
\end{equation}

We test these one by one after restriction to \(Q_B\).

\section{Projector sector}

Since
\[
P_B|_{Q_B}=0,
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q P_B \Pi_Q=0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_P_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence \(P_B\) itself provides no tangent selector.

Next,
\[
\partial_\xi P_B
=
\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\]
Because \(z_B\perp Q_B\), one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q\,\partial_\xi P_B\,\Pi_Q=0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_dP_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus neither \(P_B\) nor \(\partial_\xi P_B\) yields a linear tangent selector.

At quadratic order,
\[
(\partial_\xi P_B)^2
=
\theta'(\xi)^2\bigl(|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|+|z_B\rangle\langle z_B|\bigr),
\]
so after tangent projection
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P_B)^2\Pi_Q
=
\theta'(\xi)^2|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_dP2}
\end{equation}

Its traceless part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl(\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P_B)^2\Pi_Q\Bigr)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_dP2_tr}
\end{equation}
which is exactly the primitive Branch B carrier, not a linear Branch A carrier.

\section{Condensate sector}

The background condensate bilinear is
\[
\Psi_B\Psi_B^\dagger
=
|\phi_0|^2 P_B.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q(\Psi_B\Psi_B^\dagger)\Pi_Q=0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_PsiPsi_zero}
\end{equation}

Similarly, any scalar condensate invariant such as
\[
\Psi_B^\dagger\Psi_B=|\phi_0|^2
\]
acts only as a multiple of the identity in fluctuation space and cannot distinguish \(e_1\) from \(e_2\).

Hence no lowest-order condensate scalar can generate \(r_3\neq 0\).

\section{Volumetric scalar sector}

The background scalar \(\sigma_B\) is a scalar under tangent \(SO(2)\).
Thus any local operator built only from \(\sigma_B\) and scalar contractions contributes only
\[
\propto \mathbf 1_2
\]
on \(Q_B\). Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_B\text{-sector cannot generate a tangent }\Sigma_3\text{ selector at lowest local order.}
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_sigma_no}
\end{equation}

\section{Heavy carrier sector}

Now test the existing heavy carrier \(X_i^a\).

At lowest order in the present construction, the background \(X_{i,B}^a\) is either zero or isotropically integrated out.
Thus the only available local tensor from the \(X\)-sector before introducing any extra anisotropic kernel is
\[
X_i^aX_i^a,
\]
or isotropic quadratic kernels.

After tangent projection, such terms again produce only
\[
\propto \mathbf 1_2
\]
or the already-known transverse \(E/O\) structures, but no longitudinal \(\Sigma_3\) selector linear in \(\theta'\).

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the existing lowest-order }X\text{-sector does not generate }r_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_X_no}
\end{equation}

\section{Exhaustion theorem}

Collecting the results:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(P_B\) gives zero on \(Q_B\);
\item \(\partial_\xi P_B\) gives zero on \(Q_B\);
\item \((\partial_\xi P_B)^2\) gives \(\theta'^2\Sigma_3\), i.e. only the primitive Branch B carrier;
\item \(\Psi_B\Psi_B^\dagger\) gives zero on \(Q_B\);
\item scalar condensate and scalar volumetric terms give only \(\mathbf 1_2\);
\item the existing lowest-order heavy-carrier sector gives no linear longitudinal selector.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{No explicit local tangent }SO(2)\text{-breaking longitudinal selector can be built at lowest local order from the existing TECT variables alone.}
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_main}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_3=0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_r3_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus Branch A is excluded at this level.

\section{Forced branch}

Since the primitive carrier survives through
\[
\Bigl(\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P_B)^2\Pi_Q\Bigr)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'^2\Sigma_3,
\]
the surviving longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_lambda}
\end{equation}

Therefore the theory is forced onto Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_branchB}
\end{equation}

\section{Final reduced PDE at this order}

Including the already-constructed transverse completion,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:Exhaust_finalPDE}
\end{equation}

\section{Sharp remaining possibility}

The only way to reopen Branch A is to add a genuinely new local operator whose tangent reduction is not generated by the algebra of
\[
(P_B,\partial_\xi P_B,\Psi_B,\sigma_B,X_B)
\]
at lowest order and that produces a linear
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3
\]
selector.
Without such a new operator, Branch B is exact at this order.

\section{Final Summary}

At lowest local order, using only the existing TECT variables
\[
(\Psi,\ P,\ \sigma,\ X_i^a),
\]
one finds:

\[
\Pi_QP_B\Pi_Q=0,
\qquad
\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P_B)\Pi_Q=0,
\qquad
\Pi_Q(\Psi_B\Psi_B^\dagger)\Pi_Q=0.
\]

Scalar condensate and volumetric terms contribute only multiples of \(\mathbf 1_2\) on \(Q_B\).
The existing lowest-order heavy-carrier sector also gives no linear longitudinal selector.

The first nontrivial traceless tangent term is
\[
\Bigl(\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P_B)^2\Pi_Q\Bigr)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'^2\Sigma_3,
\]
which is exactly the primitive Branch B carrier.

Therefore no explicit local tangent \(SO(2)\)-breaking longitudinal selector can be built at lowest local order from the existing TECT variables alone:
\[
\boxed{
r_3=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\]

Since the primitive carrier survives,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\]
the theory is forced onto Branch B at this order.

Hence the reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

So the only way to realize Branch A is to add a genuinely new local operator beyond the existing lowest-order TECT variable algebra.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Higher-order local operator test for Branch A}

\section{Goal}

We now test whether higher-order local operators built from the existing TECT variables can generate
a Branch A longitudinal selector
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
\]

We restrict to local operators formed from the existing lowest-order variable algebra:
\[
(P,\partial_\xi P,\Psi^\dagger\Psi,\sigma,X_i^a),
\]
with only isotropic scalar contractions and without introducing any explicit tangent-frame selector.

\section{Basic tangent algebra}

Define
\[
Q_B=\mathrm{span}\{e_1,e_2\},
\qquad
\Pi_Q=|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|+|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|.
\]

For the real defect representative, we already have
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_QP\Pi_Q=0,
\qquad
\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P)\Pi_Q=0.
}
\label{eq:HO_basic_zero}
\end{equation}

The first nontrivial tangent operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D:=\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P)^2\Pi_Q
=
\theta'(\xi)^2|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|.
}
\label{eq:HO_D_def}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\Sigma_3\bigr).
}
\label{eq:HO_D_split}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire nontrivial tangent algebra generated by the existing variables begins with \(D\), not with \(\partial_\xi P\).

\section{Powers of the basic tangent operator}

Since
\[
|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|
\]
is a rank-one projector, one has
\[
D^n=\theta'(\xi)^{2n}|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D^n
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^{2n}}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\Sigma_3\bigr),
\qquad n\ge 1.
}
\label{eq:HO_Dn}
\end{equation}

Its traceless part is always
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(D^n)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^{2n}}{2}\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:HO_Dn_tr}
\end{equation}

Hence every traceless tangent operator generated by powers of the existing algebra is proportional to
\[
\theta'(\xi)^{2n}\Sigma_3,
\qquad n\ge 1.
\]

\section{General higher-order isotropic local operator}

Consider any local isotropic scalar density
\[
\mathcal O_{\mathrm{iso}}(P,\partial P,\Psi^\dagger\Psi,\sigma,X)
\]
built polynomially from the existing variables and their contractions.

After restriction to \(Q_B\), every contribution to its tangent Hessian is generated by products of:

\[
\Pi_Q,\qquad D,\qquad \text{scalar functions of }(\theta,\phi_0,\sigma_B,\ldots).
\]

Therefore the general tangent Hessian contribution has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_Q^{\mathrm{iso}}
=
A_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2+\sum_{n\ge 1}A_n(\xi)D^n.
}
\label{eq:HO_RQ_general}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:HO_Dn},
\begin{align}
R_Q^{\mathrm{iso}}
&=
A_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
\sum_{n\ge 1}
A_n(\xi)\frac{\theta'(\xi)^{2n}}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\Sigma_3\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&=
\Bigl[
A_0(\xi)+\frac12\sum_{n\ge 1}A_n(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^{2n}
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_2
+
\frac12\sum_{n\ge 1}A_n(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^{2n}\Sigma_3.
\label{eq:HO_RQ_expand}
\end{align}

Hence the traceless part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_Q^{\mathrm{iso}})_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\sum_{n\ge 1}A_n(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^{2n}\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:HO_RQ_tr}
\end{equation}

\section{No linear Branch A term}

Equation \eqref{eq:HO_RQ_tr} shows that every traceless tangent contribution generated by the existing isotropic local algebra is an even power series in \(\theta'(\xi)\):
\[
\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3,\quad
\theta'(\xi)^4\Sigma_3,\quad
\theta'(\xi)^6\Sigma_3,\ \dots
\]

Therefore there is no term proportional to
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
\]

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\label{eq:HO_noA}
\end{equation}
to all orders within the existing isotropic local variable algebra.

\section{Worldvolume transport consequence}

The first-order transport kernel always carries one extra odd normal factor \(\theta'(\xi)\):
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]
Thus the higher-order traceless tangent contributions produce
\[
\theta'(\xi)\cdot \theta'(\xi)^{2n}\Sigma_3
=
\theta'(\xi)^{2n+1}\Sigma_3.
\]

Hence the allowed longitudinal channels are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)^3\Sigma_3,\qquad
\theta'(\xi)^5\Sigma_3,\qquad
\theta'(\xi)^7\Sigma_3,\ \dots
}
\label{eq:HO_allowed_long}
\end{equation}
but never
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:HO_forbidden_long}
\end{equation}

Therefore Branch A remains excluded, while Branch B and its higher odd corrections survive.

\section{Higher-order corrected longitudinal coefficient}

The most general longitudinal coefficient allowed by the existing isotropic local algebra is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(2)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^5
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(3)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^7
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:HO_a3_series}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}I_3
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(2)}}{2}I_5
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(3)}}{2}I_7
+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:HO_lambda_series}
\end{equation}
where
\[
I_{2n+1}:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^{2n+1}.
\]

\section{Conclusion}

Thus higher-order local operators built only from the existing isotropic TECT variable algebra do not reopen Branch A.

They only renormalize Branch B by adding higher odd-power primitive longitudinal terms.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Within the existing isotropic local TECT algebra, Branch B is stable to all local higher-order corrections.}
}
\label{eq:HO_branchB_stable}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Using only the existing TECT variables and isotropic local scalar contractions, the basic tangent algebra is generated by
\[
\Pi_Q,\qquad
D=\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P)^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'^2}{2}(\mathbf 1_2+\Sigma_3).
\]

Hence every traceless tangent operator built from this algebra is of the form
\[
(R_Q^{\mathrm{iso}})_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\sum_{n\ge 1}A_n(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^{2n}\Sigma_3.
\]

Therefore no linear longitudinal selector
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3
\]
can ever appear.

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\]
to all orders inside the existing isotropic local variable algebra.

The transport kernel always contributes one extra odd factor \(\theta'(\xi)\), so the allowed longitudinal channels are only
\[
\theta'^3\Sigma_3,\qquad
\theta'^5\Sigma_3,\qquad
\theta'^7\Sigma_3,\ \dots
\]

Thus higher-order local corrections do not reopen Branch A.
They only renormalize Branch B.

So Branch B is stable to all local higher-order corrections built from the existing isotropic TECT variable algebra.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exhaustive loophole classification beyond the existing isotropic local TECT algebra}

\section{Goal}

We have already shown that within the existing isotropic local TECT algebra,
no linear longitudinal selector
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3
\]
can be generated.
Hence Branch A is impossible there, while Branch B survives.

We now classify all logically possible loopholes that could evade this result.

\section{Exact statement to be evaded}

The result to evade is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\label{eq:Loop_target}
\end{equation}
for every local isotropic operator built from the existing variable algebra
\[
(P,\partial P,\Psi^\dagger\Psi,\sigma,X_i^a).
\]

Thus any loophole must produce a tangent Hessian contribution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_A^\mu(\xi)\supset \theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Loop_need}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, it must generate a traceless tangent selector already at linear derivative order.

\section{Logical possibilities}

At the microscopic level there are only four logically distinct possibilities.

\subsection{Loophole I: explicit local tangent frame selector}

The full action may contain a genuinely new local operator \(R_Q\) on the tangent bundle with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_Q=r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3,
\qquad
r_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Loop_I}
\end{equation}

This is the direct Type II frame-selector loophole.
If present, Branch A is immediately possible.

\paragraph{Status.}
This operator is not present in the existing lowest-order TECT variable algebra.
Therefore Loophole I is absent in the present construction.

\subsection{Loophole II: non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement}

The full action may contain a higher-derivative refinement whose tangent reduction is not generated by the isotropic local algebra and whose first-order Hessian contributes
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
\]

Schematically, this would mean a term
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{\mathrm{ref}}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Pi_Q\,\delta^2\mathcal O_{\mathrm{ref}}\,\Pi_Q
\supset
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Loop_II}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Status.}
This cannot arise from isotropic local scalar contractions of the existing variable algebra,
because those generate only even powers of the basic tangent projector \(D\sim \theta'^2(\mathbf 1_2+\Sigma_3)\).
Therefore Loophole II is absent unless one adds a genuinely non-isotropic refinement beyond the existing algebra.

\subsection{Loophole III: nonlocal tangent memory operator}

The full theory may contain a nonlocal operator along the normal direction \(\xi\), for example
\[
\int d\xi\,d\xi'\;K(\xi,\xi')\,\partial_\xi P(\xi)\,\partial_{\xi'}P(\xi'),
\]
or an equivalent nonlocal transport kernel.
Such an operator is not generated by the local algebra and may effectively define a preferred tangent frame.

In that case the tangent Hessian need not be a local polynomial in \(D\), and a linear \(\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3\) term may appear.

\paragraph{Status.}
This loophole is excluded if one assumes the full effective action is local in the defect neighborhood.
The current TECT construction is organized as a local effective theory, so Loophole III is absent under the locality assumption.

\subsection{Loophole IV: spontaneous tangent nematic order}

The full theory may generate an additional background expectation value \(N_Q\) in the tangent bundle such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_Q=n_0\mathbf 1_2+n_3\Sigma_3,
\qquad
n_3\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Loop_IV}
\end{equation}

This would spontaneously break the local tangent \(SO(2)\) symmetry down to a selected frame and act exactly as a Branch A carrier.

\paragraph{Status.}
This requires an independent tangent-nematic condensate sector or a spontaneous instability in the full microscopic Hessian.
No such sector has been identified in the present TECT construction.
So Loophole IV is absent unless a new spontaneous tangent-order parameter is introduced or dynamically found.

\section{Exhaustion theorem}

Therefore the loopholes are exhausted by the four classes above.

If the full complete TECT action satisfies:

\begin{enumerate}
\item locality in the defect neighborhood,
\item no explicit local tangent frame selector,
\item no genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement,
\item no spontaneous tangent nematic order,
\end{enumerate}

then none of Loopholes I--IV is available.

Hence the previous no-go result extends to the full theory:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\label{eq:Loop_noA_full}
\end{equation}
and Branch A is excluded.

\section{Exact surviving longitudinal structure}

Under these assumptions, the longitudinal transport sector is necessarily an odd-power series:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(2)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^5
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(3)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^7
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:Loop_a3_odd}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}I_3
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(2)}}{2}I_5
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(3)}}{2}I_7
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:Loop_lambda_odd}
\end{equation}

Thus Branch B is not merely the lowest-order outcome; it is the exact stable branch of the full theory under the assumptions above.

\section{Final reduced PDE under loophole exclusion}

If in addition the transverse sector remains nonzero,
\[
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
\]
then the reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:Loop_final_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}I_3+\frac{\lambda_c^{(2)}}{2}I_5+\cdots,
\qquad
\alpha\neq 0 \text{ or } \beta\neq 0.
\]

\section{Sharpest honest conclusion}

Therefore the branch problem is now reduced to the following exact alternative:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Either the full complete TECT action contains one of Loopholes I--IV, in which case Branch A is possible,}
}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{none of them is present, in which case Branch B is exact to all local orders.}
}
\end{equation}

In the present construction, no explicit evidence for any of Loopholes I--IV has been found.
Hence the strongest current microscopic conclusion is that Branch B is the natural exact branch of TECT unless genuinely new structure is added.

\section{Final Summary}

To evade the Branch B no-go, the full theory must realize at least one of the following loopholes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{I: explicit local tangent frame selector;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{II: genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{III: nonlocal tangent memory operator;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{IV: spontaneous tangent nematic order.}
}
\]

These four possibilities exhaust the ways to generate a linear longitudinal selector
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
\]

If none of I--IV is present, then
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\]
exactly, and the longitudinal sector is an odd-power Branch B series:
\[
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}\theta'^3
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(2)}}{2}\theta'^5
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(3)}}{2}\theta'^7
+\cdots.
\]

Therefore Branch B is exact to all local orders under the assumptions:
locality, tangent \(SO(2)\) invariance, and no new tangent-anisotropy carrier.

So the remaining microscopic question is now maximally sharp:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the true full complete TECT action realize any of Loopholes I--IV?}
}
\]

If not, then the final reduced PDE is on Branch B exactly.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Elimination of loopholes I, III, IV and reduction to loophole II}

\section{Goal}

We now test the four possible loopholes that could evade the Branch B no-go:

\[
\mathrm{I}:\ \text{explicit local tangent frame selector},
\qquad
\mathrm{II}:\ \text{genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement},
\]
\[
\mathrm{III}:\ \text{nonlocal tangent memory operator},
\qquad
\mathrm{IV}:\ \text{spontaneous tangent nematic order}.
\]

We show that, within the current TECT framework and assumptions already used in the construction,
Loopholes I, III, and IV are excluded, so that only Loophole II remains.

\section{Loophole I: explicit local tangent frame selector}

Loophole I would require an operator \(R_Q\) on the tangent bundle such that
\[
R_Q=r_0\mathbf 1_2+r_3\Sigma_3,
\qquad
r_3\neq 0,
\]
already at the microscopic local level.

However, in the present TECT variable set
\[
(\Psi,\ P,\ \sigma,\ X_i^a),
\]
there is no independent field whose background value selects \(e_1\) over \(e_2\) at zeroth derivative order.

Indeed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(P_B\) vanishes on \(Q_B\):
\[
\Pi_QP_B\Pi_Q=0;
\]
\item \(\Psi_B\Psi_B^\dagger\propto P_B\), so again
\[
\Pi_Q(\Psi_B\Psi_B^\dagger)\Pi_Q=0;
\]
\item \(\sigma_B\) is a scalar, hence contributes only \(\propto \mathbf 1_2\);
\item the present \(X\)-sector has no independent tangent-frame background expectation value.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore no explicit local tangent frame selector exists in the present TECT field content.

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Loophole\ I\ is\ absent.}
}
\label{eq:elim_I}
\end{equation}

\section{Loophole III: nonlocal tangent memory operator}

Loophole III would require a nonlocal operator along the normal direction, schematically
\[
\int d\xi\,d\xi'\,K(\xi,\xi')\,\mathcal O(\xi)\mathcal O(\xi'),
\]
whose tangent reduction effectively defines a preferred frame.

But the entire present TECT construction is organized as a local effective theory in the defect neighborhood:
the action is assumed to be a local functional of the fields and finitely many derivatives,
and all previous Hessian reductions, transport kernels, and low-mode projections rely on this locality.

Thus, if we keep the current local-action framework, nonlocal memory operators are excluded by construction.

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Loophole\ III\ is\ absent\ under\ the\ locality\ assumption.}
}
\label{eq:elim_III}
\end{equation}

\section{Loophole IV: spontaneous tangent nematic order}

Loophole IV would require an additional tangent order parameter
\[
N_Q=n_0\mathbf 1_2+n_3\Sigma_3,
\qquad
n_3\neq 0,
\]
generated spontaneously by the full microscopic dynamics.

For this to occur, at least one of the following must be present:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an independent microscopic tangent-nematic field;
\item a tachyonic instability in the symmetric-traceless tangent channel;
\item a quartic stabilization mechanism selecting a nonzero \(\Sigma_3\)-expectation value.
\end{enumerate}

None of these has been identified in the current TECT construction.

More importantly, the present low-energy tangent sector is organized around local \(SO(2)\)-invariant quadratic kernels.
Such kernels are proportional to \(\mathbf 1_2\) and do not by themselves generate a spontaneous \(\Sigma_3\) condensate.

Therefore spontaneous tangent nematic order is not available in the present theory unless one enlarges the microscopic order-parameter content or explicitly demonstrates a symmetry-breaking instability.

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Loophole\ IV\ is\ absent\ in\ the\ current\ TECT\ framework.}
}
\label{eq:elim_IV}
\end{equation}

\section{Remaining loophole II}

The only loophole not yet excluded is Loophole II:
a genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement whose tangent Hessian contributes
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3
\]
without being reducible to the existing isotropic local algebra.

That is, one would need a term
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{\mathrm{ref,new}}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Pi_Q\,\delta^2\mathcal O_{\mathrm{ref,new}}\,\Pi_Q
\supset
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:elim_II}
\end{equation}

This cannot come from the already analyzed isotropic local algebra, but it could arise from a genuinely new refined operator not yet classified.

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Loophole\ II\ is\ the\ only\ remaining\ microscopic\ possibility.}
}
\label{eq:elim_only_II}
\end{equation}

\section{Consequence for the branch problem}

If Loophole II is also absent, then all loopholes I--IV are eliminated, and Branch B is exact:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\quad\text{to all local orders,}
}
\label{eq:elim_branchB_exact}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\frac{\lambda_c^{(2)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^5
+
\cdots.
}
\label{eq:elim_a3_series}
\end{equation}

Thus the reduced PDE is exactly of Branch B type.

\section{Sharp final reduction}

Hence the full branch problem is now reduced from four possibilities to one:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the true full complete TECT action contain a genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement?}
}
\label{eq:elim_final_question}
\end{equation}

If no, then Branch B is exact.

If yes, then one must compute its tangent Hessian projection explicitly and test whether it generates
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

Within the current TECT framework:

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Loophole\ I\ (explicit\ frame\ selector)\ is\ absent,}
}
\]
because no existing field in \((\Psi,P,\sigma,X)\) selects \(e_1\) over \(e_2\) at zeroth derivative order.

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Loophole\ III\ (nonlocal\ memory)\ is\ absent,}
}
\]
because the present TECT construction is explicitly local in the defect neighborhood.

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Loophole\ IV\ (spontaneous\ tangent\ nematic)\ is\ absent,}
}
\]
because no independent tangent-nematic order parameter or symmetry-breaking instability has been identified in the current theory.

Therefore the only remaining loophole is

\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Loophole\ II:\ genuinely\ non\text{-}isotropic\ higher\text{-}derivative\ refinement.}
}
\]

So the entire branch problem is now reduced to one final microscopic question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the true full complete TECT action contain a genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement that produces }
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3\ ?
}
\]

If not, then
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\]
to all local orders and Branch B is exact.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exhaustion and elimination of loophole II}

\section{Problem}

We now classify all possible genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinements built from the existing
TECT fields
\[
(\Psi,P,\sigma,X_i^a)
\]
and test whether any of them can generate a linear longitudinal tangent selector
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
\]

Equivalently, we ask whether any local scalar invariant built from the existing field content can contribute
to the tangent Hessian a term
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{II}}(\xi)\supset \theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:L2_goal}
\end{equation}

\section{Representation-theoretic criterion}

On the tangent bundle \(Q_B\), the operator \(\Sigma_3\) is a symmetric traceless rank-two object under the local tangent \(SO(2)\).
Therefore, a necessary condition for \eqref{eq:L2_goal} is that the microscopic invariant contain, before final scalar contraction,
a tangent spin-2 carrier.

Thus loophole II can exist only if the existing field algebra generates a local symmetric-traceless tangent tensor at linear derivative order.

\section{Available derivative building blocks}

At lowest nontrivial orders, the independent local derivative building blocks are:

\[
\partial_\mu P,\qquad
\partial_\mu\Psi,\qquad
\partial_\mu\sigma,\qquad
\partial_\mu X_i^a,
\]
and higher derivatives thereof.

After insertion of the real defect background, their tangent restrictions behave as follows.

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{$\partial_\xi P$}{dP}}

We already know
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P)\Pi_Q=0.
}
\label{eq:L2_dP_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore \(\partial_\xi P\) itself does not furnish a tangent spin-2 carrier.

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{$\partial_\xi\Psi_B$}{dPsi}}

Since
\[
\Psi_B=\phi_0 z_B,
\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1,
\]
one has
\[
\partial_\xi\Psi_B
=
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)z_B+\phi_0\theta' e_1.
\]
But a single vector in \(Q_B\) does not yet define a symmetric traceless endomorphism on \(Q_B\).
To obtain such an endomorphism one must form a bilinear, e.g.
\[
|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|.
\]
Hence the first tangent spin-2 object from the condensate gradient is again quadratic in \(\theta'\).

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{$\partial_\xi\sigma_B$}{d sigma}}

The scalar \(\sigma_B\) has no tangent index, so no tangent spin-2 carrier can be built linearly from it.

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{$\partial_\mu X_i^a$}{dX}}

The field \(X_i^a\) carries a spatial index \(i\) and internal index \(a\), but no tangent bundle endomorphism structure by itself.
To generate a tangent \(\Sigma_3\) selector from \(X\), one still needs a background-dependent map from \((i,a)\) to a symmetric-traceless endomorphism of \(Q_B\).
Within the existing isotropic algebra, that map can only come from the projector geometry, hence again from at least quadratic tangent structures.

Therefore none of the linear derivative building blocks yields a tangent spin-2 carrier at order \(\theta'\).

\section{General local scalar invariant}

Any local scalar invariant built from the existing fields has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{\mathrm{loc}}
=
\mathcal C\bigl(
P,\Psi^\dagger\Psi,\sigma,X;
\partial P,\partial\Psi,\partial\sigma,\partial X;
\partial^2 P,\partial^2\Psi,\dots
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:L2_local_general}
\end{equation}
where all free indices are fully contracted using isotropic tensors.

To contribute to \(\Sigma_3\), the second variation of \(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{loc}}\) must contain a tangent symmetric-traceless carrier.
But from the building-block analysis above, every such carrier made from the existing variable algebra starts only at quadratic tangent order.

Therefore the tangent Hessian contribution has the general structure
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(R_Q^{\mathrm{II}})_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
B_1(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3
+
B_2(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^4\Sigma_3
+
B_3(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^6\Sigma_3
+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:L2_tr_series}
\end{equation}

In particular, there is no term proportional to \(\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3\).

\section{Why higher derivatives do not help}

One may worry that higher normal derivatives such as
\[
\partial_\xi^2 P,\qquad
\partial_\xi^2\Psi,\qquad
\partial_\xi\partial_\mu P
\]
could generate a linear longitudinal selector.

But this does not happen.

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{$\partial_\xi^2 P$}{d2P}}

A direct differentiation gives
\[
\partial_\xi^2 P
=
\theta''(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)
+
\theta'^2(\cdots).
\]
The first term has the same tangent structure as \(\partial_\xi P\), hence vanishes after tangent projection:
\[
\Pi_Q\bigl[\theta''(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)\bigr]\Pi_Q=0.
\]
The remaining nonzero tangent part is again quadratic in \(\theta'\).

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{$\partial_\xi^2\Psi_B$}{d2Psi}}

Likewise,
\[
\partial_\xi^2\Psi_B
\]
contains terms proportional to \(z_B\), \(e_1\), and \(\theta'^2\) times tangent vectors.
The tangent endomorphism obtained from these terms still begins only at bilinear order in tangent vectors, hence at quadratic order in \(\theta'\).

\subsection{Mixed derivatives}

Any mixed derivative term such as
\[
\partial_\xi\partial_\mu P,\qquad
\partial_\xi\partial_\mu\Psi
\]
still contains only one tangent vector before bilinearization.
After scalar contraction, the first nonzero symmetric-traceless tangent operator again starts at quadratic tangent order.

Therefore higher derivatives do not evade the parity/representation obstruction.

\section{No-go theorem for loophole II}

Hence we obtain:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{No genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement built solely from the existing local TECT variable algebra can generate } \theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:L2_nogo}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\label{eq:L2_Lambda_zero}
\end{equation}
to all local orders within the existing field content and isotropic local scalar framework.

\section{What loophole II would actually require}

To realize loophole II for real, one would need a refinement that is not merely higher derivative, but introduces a new microscopic spin-2 tangent carrier not generated by the present local algebra.

That means a term of schematic form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{\mathrm{new}}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Pi_Q\delta^2\mathcal O_{\mathrm{new}}\Pi_Q
\supset
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:L2_newneeded}
\end{equation}
where the \(\Sigma_3\) piece is already present before the usual bilinear tangent construction.

This is no longer a refinement of the existing algebra.
It is effectively a new tangent-anisotropy carrier in disguise.

\section{Final consequence}

Therefore loophole II is also absent within the current TECT framework, provided one keeps:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the existing field content \((\Psi,P,\sigma,X)\),
\item locality,
\item isotropic scalar contractions,
\item no independent tangent-anisotropy carrier.
\end{enumerate}

Under these assumptions, all loopholes I--IV are absent, and Branch B is exact:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}\theta'^3+\frac{\lambda_c^{(2)}}{2}\theta'^5+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:L2_branchB_exact}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Loophole II asked whether a genuinely non-isotropic higher-derivative refinement built from the existing TECT fields
\[
(\Psi,P,\sigma,X)
\]
could generate a linear longitudinal selector
\[
\theta'(\xi)\Sigma_3.
\]

The answer is no.

The reason is representation-theoretic: \(\Sigma_3\) is a tangent spin-2 symmetric-traceless operator, while the existing local building blocks produce no tangent spin-2 carrier at linear derivative order.

The first nonzero tangent spin-2 object generated by the present variable algebra is always quadratic in the defect gradient:
\[
(\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P)^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
\]

Therefore every higher-order local correction built from the same algebra produces only
\[
\theta'^2\Sigma_3,\quad
\theta'^4\Sigma_3,\quad
\theta'^6\Sigma_3,\ \dots
\]
inside the tangent Hessian, and hence only
\[
\theta'^3\Sigma_3,\quad
\theta'^5\Sigma_3,\quad
\theta'^7\Sigma_3,\ \dots
\]
in the transport kernel.

So no linear Branch A term ever appears:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\]
to all local orders inside the current TECT field content and isotropic local scalar framework.

Thus loophole II is also eliminated, and Branch B becomes exact under the current assumptions.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Microscopic normalization of the exact Branch B reduced PDE}

\section{Exact Branch B longitudinal tower}

Since
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
the longitudinal coefficient is an odd-power tower:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\frac{\lambda_c^{(n)}}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^{2n+1}.
}
\label{eq:Norm_a3tower}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,a_3(\xi)
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\frac{\lambda_c^{(n)}}{2}I_{2n+1},
}
\label{eq:Norm_lambdatower}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{2n+1}
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^{2n+1}.
}
\label{eq:Norm_Iodd}
\end{equation}

At lowest order,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}I_3.
}
\label{eq:Norm_lambdaLO}
\end{equation}

\section{Transverse sector}

Likewise, the transverse sector has the expansion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_E(\xi)
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(2)}\theta'(\xi)^3\cos\theta(\xi)
+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:Norm_bE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O(\xi)
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(2)}\theta'(\xi)^3\cos\theta(\xi)
+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:Norm_bO}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(n)}J_{2n-1},
\qquad
\beta
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(n)}J_{2n-1},
}
\label{eq:Norm_alphabeta_series}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{2n-1}
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^{2n-1}\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Norm_Jodd}
\end{equation}

At lowest order,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{LO}}=\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}J_1,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{LO}}=\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}J_1.
}
\label{eq:Norm_alphaLO}
\end{equation}

\section{Canonical reduced normalization}

Introduce the effective Branch B velocities
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel:=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
v_E:=\alpha,
\qquad
v_O:=\beta.
}
\label{eq:Norm_velocities}
\end{equation}

Then the exact reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
v_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:Norm_exactPDE}
\end{equation}

At leading order this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{LO}}=\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}I_3,
\qquad
v_E^{\mathrm{LO}}=\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}J_1,
\qquad
v_O^{\mathrm{LO}}=\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}J_1.
}
\label{eq:Norm_LOvel}
\end{equation}

\section{Dirac cone normalization}

Define the transverse magnitude
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp:=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}.
}
\label{eq:Norm_vperp}
\end{equation}

Then the reduced dispersion relation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega(\mathbf p)^2
=
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:Norm_dispersion}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact Branch B reduced PDE is fully normalized by the three microscopic numbers
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel,\qquad v_E,\qquad v_O,
}
\label{eq:Norm_three}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel,\qquad v_\perp,\qquad
\varphi:=\arg(v_E+i v_O).
}
\label{eq:Norm_polar}
\end{equation}

\section{Field redefinition to canonical transverse form}

If \(v_\perp\neq 0\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\cos\varphi=\frac{v_E}{v_\perp},
\qquad
\sin\varphi=\frac{v_O}{v_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:Norm_phi}
\end{equation}

Then after a constant spinor rotation in the \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\)-plane,
the PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1')+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2')\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi'=0,
}
\label{eq:Norm_canonical}
\end{equation}
where \((p_1',p_2')\) is the rotated transverse momentum basis.

Thus \(v_O\) does not introduce a new invariant scale; it only rotates the transverse frame.
The invariant data are \(v_\parallel\) and \(v_\perp\).

\section{Final exact Branch B statement}

Therefore the exact reduced Branch B PDE of TECT is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
v_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:Norm_finalBranchB}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\frac{\lambda_c^{(n)}}{2}I_{2n+1},
\qquad
v_E
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(n)}J_{2n-1},
\qquad
v_O
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(n)}J_{2n-1}.
}
\label{eq:Norm_finalvel}
\end{equation}

Its exact nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Norm_finalnondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Once Branch A is excluded, the reduced PDE is exactly of Branch B type.

The longitudinal coefficient is an odd tower:
\[
v_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\frac{\lambda_c^{(n)}}{2}I_{2n+1},
\qquad
I_{2n+1}=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^{\,2n+1}.
\]

The transverse coefficients are
\[
v_E=\alpha
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(n)}J_{2n-1},
\qquad
v_O=\beta
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(n)}J_{2n-1},
\]
with
\[
J_{2n-1}=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^{\,2n-1}\cos\theta.
\]

Therefore the exact Branch B reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
v_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

Its invariant physical normalization is determined by
\[
v_\parallel,
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2},
\]
since \(v_O\) can be absorbed into a transverse frame rotation.

Thus the only remaining microscopic task is the quantitative evaluation of the coefficients
\[
\lambda_c^{(n)},\qquad \widetilde\Lambda_E^{(n)},\qquad \widetilde\Lambda_O^{(n)}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Dimensionless normalization and robustness of the exact Branch B PDE}

\section{Exact Branch B reduced PDE}

The exact reduced Branch B PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
v_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_BranchB}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp:=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_vperp}
\end{equation}

After a constant transverse frame rotation, \eqref{eq:Dimless_BranchB} is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1')+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2')\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi'=0.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_canonical}
\end{equation}

Thus the invariant physical data are \(v_\parallel\) and \(v_\perp\).

\section{Choice of reference scale}

Introduce a positive reference velocity \(v_*>0\).
A natural choice is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_*:=v_\perp
}
\label{eq:Dimless_vstar1}
\end{equation}
or, alternatively,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_*:=\sqrt{v_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_vstar2}
\end{equation}

Using \(v_*=v_\perp\), define the dimensionless anisotropy ratio
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho:=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_rho}
\end{equation}

Then \eqref{eq:Dimless_canonical} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_{\tilde t}
-
\rho\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_{\tilde\parallel})
-
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_{\tilde 1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{\tilde 2})\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi'=0,
}
\label{eq:Dimless_rhoPDE}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\tilde t=v_\perp t,
\qquad
\tilde x_\parallel=v_\perp x_\parallel,
\qquad
\tilde x_1=v_\perp x_1',
\qquad
\tilde x_2=v_\perp x_2'.
\]

Therefore the exact Branch B PDE is classified, up to rescaling and transverse rotation, by the single dimensionless parameter
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_single}
\end{equation}

\section{Microscopic expression for \texorpdfstring{$\rho$}{rho}}

Recall
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\frac{\lambda_c^{(n)}}{2}I_{2n+1},
\qquad
v_E
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(n)}J_{2n-1},
\qquad
v_O
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(n)}J_{2n-1}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_microvel}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{
\sum_{n\ge 1}\frac{\lambda_c^{(n)}}{2}I_{2n+1}
}{
\sqrt{
\left(\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(n)}J_{2n-1}\right)^2
+
\left(\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(n)}J_{2n-1}\right)^2
}
}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_rho_micro}
\end{equation}

At leading order,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\frac{\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}I_3}{
J_1\sqrt{(\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)})^2+(\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)})^2}
}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_rho_LO}
\end{equation}

\section{Dimensionless robustness parameters}

Let
\[
\delta v_\parallel,\qquad \delta v_E,\qquad \delta v_O
\]
denote corrections from higher-order operators, truncation error, or microscopic uncertainty.

Define the relative error parameters
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\parallel:=\frac{|\delta v_\parallel|}{|v_\parallel|},
\qquad
\varepsilon_\perp:=\frac{\sqrt{(\delta v_E)^2+(\delta v_O)^2}}{v_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_eps}
\end{equation}

Then the reduced PDE remains Dirac-nondegenerate provided
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\parallel<1,
\qquad
\varepsilon_\perp<1.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_eps_cond}
\end{equation}

Indeed, if \(\varepsilon_\parallel<1\), then
\[
|v_\parallel+\delta v_\parallel|
\ge |v_\parallel|-|\delta v_\parallel|
=
|v_\parallel|(1-\varepsilon_\parallel)>0.
\]
Likewise, if \(\varepsilon_\perp<1\), then
\[
v_\perp^{\mathrm{new}}
\ge v_\perp-\sqrt{(\delta v_E)^2+(\delta v_O)^2}
=
v_\perp(1-\varepsilon_\perp)>0.
\]

Thus the nondegeneracy condition is stable.

\section{Robustness in microscopic form}

Split the coefficients into leading and higher-order parts:
\[
v_\parallel=v_\parallel^{\mathrm{LO}}+\Delta v_\parallel,
\qquad
v_E=v_E^{\mathrm{LO}}+\Delta v_E,
\qquad
v_O=v_O^{\mathrm{LO}}+\Delta v_O.
\]

Then a sufficient robustness criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta v_\parallel|<|v_\parallel^{\mathrm{LO}}|,
\qquad
\sqrt{(\Delta v_E)^2+(\Delta v_O)^2}
<
\sqrt{(v_E^{\mathrm{LO}})^2+(v_O^{\mathrm{LO}})^2}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_robust_LO}
\end{equation}

In terms of the microscopic series, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_{n\ge 2}\frac{\lambda_c^{(n)}}{2}I_{2n+1}
\right|
<
\left|
\frac{\lambda_c^{(1)}}{2}I_3
\right|,
}
\label{eq:Dimless_long_robust}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sqrt{
\left(\sum_{n\ge 2}\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(n)}J_{2n-1}\right)^2
+
\left(\sum_{n\ge 2}\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(n)}J_{2n-1}\right)^2
}
<
J_1\sqrt{(\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)})^2+(\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)})^2}.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_trans_robust}
\end{equation}

\section{Universality classes}

The exact Branch B reduced PDE is naturally organized into the following universality classes.

\paragraph{Class I: isotropic Dirac cone.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho=1.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_class1}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Class II: anisotropic but nondegenerate Dirac cone.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<|\rho|<\infty,
\qquad
\rho\neq 1.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_class2}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Class III: longitudinally collapsed limit.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho=0.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_class3}
\end{equation}
This is excluded for a genuine Branch B Dirac phase.

\paragraph{Class IV: transversely collapsed limit.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp=0.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_class4}
\end{equation}
This is excluded by transverse nondegeneracy.

Therefore the exact Branch B Dirac phase is precisely
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho\in \mathbb R\setminus\{0\},
\qquad
v_\perp>0.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_phase}
\end{equation}

\section{Final exact Branch B statement}

Thus the exact Branch B reduced PDE is completely characterized by:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{one dimensionless anisotropy parameter }\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp},
}
\label{eq:Dimless_final1}
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the robustness conditions }
\varepsilon_\parallel<1,\qquad \varepsilon_\perp<1.
}
\label{eq:Dimless_final2}
\end{equation}

Under these conditions, the TECT reduced Branch B phase is stable under all local higher-order corrections from the existing isotropic local variable algebra.

\section{Final Summary}

After excluding Branch A, the exact reduced PDE is of Branch B type and is fully characterized by
\[
v_\parallel,\qquad
v_E,\qquad
v_O.
\]

Up to transverse frame rotation, the invariant physical data reduce to
\[
v_\parallel,
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}.
\]

Therefore, after rescaling, the exact Branch B PDE is classified by the single dimensionless anisotropy parameter
\[
\boxed{
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
}
\]

Microscopically,
\[
v_\parallel
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\frac{\lambda_c^{(n)}}{2}I_{2n+1},
\qquad
v_E
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(n)}J_{2n-1},
\qquad
v_O
=
\sum_{n\ge 1}\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(n)}J_{2n-1}.
\]

A sufficient robustness criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\parallel<1,
\qquad
\varepsilon_\perp<1,
}
\]
or equivalently
\[
|\Delta v_\parallel|<|v_\parallel^{\mathrm{LO}}|,
\qquad
\sqrt{(\Delta v_E)^2+(\Delta v_O)^2}
<
\sqrt{(v_E^{\mathrm{LO}})^2+(v_O^{\mathrm{LO}})^2}.
\]

Thus the exact TECT Branch B phase is stable and universal up to the single anisotropy ratio \(\rho\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Leading estimate of the anisotropy ratio}

Using the explicit concrete Class II coefficients,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa,
\]
we obtain
\[
v_\perp
=
\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,|\theta_0\kappa|\,\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}.
\]

Hence the leading anisotropy ratio is
\[
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{v_\perp}
=
-\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{g_c}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}\,
\frac{\theta_0^3\kappa^3}{|\theta_0\kappa|}.
}
\]

Equivalently, in magnitude,
\[
\boxed{
|\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Physical regimes of the anisotropy ratio \texorpdfstring{$\rho$}{rho}}

\section{Definition}

The exact Branch B reduced PDE is characterized by
\[
v_\parallel,\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2},
\qquad
\rho:=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
\]

At leading order in the explicit concrete Class II realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:rho_LO_again}
\end{equation}

Thus the anisotropy is controlled by two factors:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the microscopic coupling ratio
\[
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}},
\]
\item the geometric small parameter
\[
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{Regime I: strongly transverse-dominated cone}

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\ll 1,
}
\label{eq:rho_small}
\end{equation}
then
\[
|v_\parallel|\ll v_\perp.
\]

The dispersion is
\[
\omega(\mathbf p)^2
=
v_\parallel^2p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2(p_1^2+p_2^2),
\]
so longitudinal propagation is parametrically slower than transverse propagation.

This means:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the cone is highly anisotropic;
\item the defect supports almost two-dimensional transverse Dirac propagation;
\item longitudinal motion is a weak primitive correction.
\end{enumerate}

In the explicit Branch B realization, this is the generic regime whenever
\[
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}
\not\gg (\theta_0\kappa)^{-2}.
\]

\section{Regime II: balanced anisotropic Dirac cone}

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\sim 1,
}
\label{eq:rho_order1}
\end{equation}
then longitudinal and transverse velocities are of the same order:
\[
|v_\parallel|\sim v_\perp.
\]

The cone is still generally anisotropic, but not parametrically so.
This is the regime in which the reduced PDE most closely resembles a conventional three-directional Dirac operator with finite anisotropy.

To obtain this in Branch B, one needs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}
\sim
(\theta_0\kappa)^{-2}.
}
\label{eq:rho_balanced_condition}
\end{equation}

So the primitive longitudinal channel must be strongly enhanced relative to the transverse channel.

\section{Regime III: longitudinally dominated cone}

If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\gg 1,
}
\label{eq:rho_large}
\end{equation}
then
\[
