|v_\parallel|\gg v_\perp.
\]

The cone is now elongated in the transverse directions and dominated by the longitudinal channel.

Inside the present explicit Branch B realization, this regime is unnatural unless the microscopic ratio
\[
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}
\]
is extraordinarily large, since the geometric suppression factor \((\theta_0\kappa)^2\) works against the longitudinal channel.

Therefore \(|\rho|\gg 1\) is not the natural expectation for the concrete Class II Branch B phase.

\section{Natural TECT expectation}

Combining the explicit coefficient hierarchy with \eqref{eq:rho_LO_again}, the natural expectation in the present TECT Branch B construction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\ll 1.
}
\label{eq:rho_natural}
\end{equation}

That is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the natural Branch B phase is a strongly anisotropic Dirac cone with parametrically suppressed longitudinal velocity.}
}
\label{eq:rho_natural_words}
\end{equation}

\section{Physical interpretation}

Hence the three regimes have the following meanings:

\paragraph{Regime I: \(\rho\ll 1\).}
Transverse-dominated Dirac propagation.
This is the natural explicit Branch B regime.

\paragraph{Regime II: \(\rho\sim 1\).}
Balanced anisotropic Dirac cone.
This requires strong enhancement of the primitive longitudinal carrier.

\paragraph{Regime III: \(\rho\gg 1\).}
Longitudinally dominated propagation.
This is highly non-generic in the present Branch B construction.

\section{Robustness view}

Since the Branch B longitudinal sector starts at primitive order while the transverse sector starts at lower order,
small corrections generically preserve the hierarchy
\[
|v_\parallel|<v_\perp.
\]
Thus the \(\rho\ll 1\) regime is not only natural but also robust against moderate higher-order corrections.

\section{Final concise conclusion}

Therefore the present explicit TECT Branch B construction predicts:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{generic phase: }\rho\ll 1,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{fine-tuned phase: }\rho\sim 1,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{unnatural phase: }\rho\gg 1.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The anisotropy ratio is
\[
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp},
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}.
\]

In the explicit Branch B realization,
\[
|\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\rho\ll 1
}
\]
means a strongly transverse-dominated Dirac cone and is the natural generic regime;

\[
\boxed{
\rho\sim 1
}
\]
means a balanced anisotropic Dirac cone and requires enhancement of the primitive longitudinal channel;

\[
\boxed{
\rho\gg 1
}
\]
means a longitudinally dominated cone and is non-generic in the present Branch B construction.

Hence the natural TECT expectation is
\[
\boxed{
\rho\ll 1.
}
\]
So the present explicit Branch B phase predicts a parametrically suppressed longitudinal velocity relative to the transverse Dirac velocity.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Three physical predictions of the exact Branch B phase}

\section{Starting point}

The exact reduced Branch B PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
v_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:Pred_start}
\end{equation}

After a constant transverse frame rotation, this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1')+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2')\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi'=0,
}
\label{eq:Pred_canonical}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2},
\qquad
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:Pred_rho}
\end{equation}

The dispersion relation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega(\mathbf p)^2
=
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1'^2+p_2'^2).
}
\label{eq:Pred_dispersion}
\end{equation}

\section{Prediction 1: strongly anisotropic Dirac cone}

The first direct prediction is the shape of the low-energy cone.

Constant-energy surfaces satisfy
\[
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2 p_\perp^2=\omega^2,
\]
hence the momentum-space semi-axes are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_\parallel^{\max}=\frac{\omega}{|v_\parallel|},
\qquad
p_\perp^{\max}=\frac{\omega}{v_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:Pred_axes}
\end{equation}

Therefore the cone anisotropy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{p_\parallel^{\max}}{p_\perp^{\max}}
=
\frac{v_\perp}{|v_\parallel|}
=
\frac{1}{|\rho|}.
}
\label{eq:Pred_axisratio}
\end{equation}

In the natural TECT Branch B regime \(|\rho|\ll 1\), the cone is highly elongated in the longitudinal momentum direction and strongly compressed in velocity space along the longitudinal direction.

Thus the first prediction is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The low-energy Dirac cone is strongly anisotropic, with aspect ratio } \sim |\rho|^{-1}\gg 1.
}
\label{eq:Pred1}
\end{equation}

\section{Prediction 2: quasi-two-dimensional low-energy transport}

The group velocity is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbf v_g
=
\nabla_{\mathbf p}\omega
=
\frac{1}{\omega}
\Bigl(
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel,\,
v_\perp^2 p_1',\,
v_\perp^2 p_2'
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Pred_groupvel}
\end{equation}

Hence the characteristic velocity scales are
\[
|v_{g,\parallel}|\sim |v_\parallel|,
\qquad
|v_{g,\perp}|\sim v_\perp.
\]

If \(|\rho|\ll 1\), then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|v_{g,\parallel}|\ll |v_{g,\perp}|.
}
\label{eq:Pred_vsupp}
\end{equation}

Therefore low-energy propagation is effectively quasi-two-dimensional:
modes spread rapidly in the transverse defect plane but only weakly along the longitudinal direction.

Thus the second prediction is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Low-energy transport is quasi-two-dimensional, with parametrically suppressed longitudinal propagation.}
}
\label{eq:Pred2}
\end{equation}

\section{Prediction 3: robust universality controlled by a single anisotropy parameter}

Up to transverse rotation and overall rescaling, the exact reduced PDE is characterized by the single dimensionless parameter
\[
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
\]

Therefore all low-energy observables that depend only on the local cone geometry must collapse onto a one-parameter family.

For example:

\begin{itemize}
\item cone aspect ratio;
\item directional group velocity ratio;
\item directional response anisotropy;
\item scaling of longitudinal versus transverse spectral broadening.
\end{itemize}

All such quantities are functions only of \(\rho\).

Thus the third prediction is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The entire low-energy Branch B phenomenology is universal up to one dimensionless parameter } \rho.
}
\label{eq:Pred3}
\end{equation}

\section{Leading microscopic estimate}

Using the explicit concrete Class II leading coefficients,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:Pred_rhoLO}
\end{equation}

Hence, unless the primitive longitudinal coupling is strongly enhanced,
the natural expectation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\ll 1.
}
\label{eq:Pred_rhosmall}
\end{equation}

So all three predictions above are expected to appear in the generic explicit Branch B regime.

\section{Compressed final statement}

Therefore the exact Branch B phase predicts:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) a highly anisotropic Dirac cone,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) quasi-two-dimensional low-energy transport,}
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(iii) universality controlled by the single anisotropy ratio }\rho.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The exact Branch B reduced PDE implies three direct physical predictions.

First, the dispersion
\[
\omega^2=v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2 p_\perp^2
\]
gives a strongly anisotropic Dirac cone with aspect ratio
\[
\frac{p_\parallel^{\max}}{p_\perp^{\max}}=\frac{1}{|\rho|},
\qquad
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
\]

Second, the group velocities satisfy
\[
|v_{g,\parallel}|\sim |v_\parallel|,
\qquad
|v_{g,\perp}|\sim v_\perp,
\]
so for the natural regime \(|\rho|\ll 1\), low-energy transport is quasi-two-dimensional with suppressed longitudinal propagation.

Third, after transverse rotation and rescaling, the entire low-energy phenomenology depends only on the single dimensionless anisotropy parameter
\[
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
\]

Using the explicit concrete Class II leading coefficients,
\[
|\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
\]
so the natural expectation is
\[
|\rho|\ll 1.
\]

Therefore the generic explicit Branch B phase predicts:
\[
\boxed{
\text{a highly anisotropic Dirac cone,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{quasi-two-dimensional low-energy transport,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{and one-parameter universality controlled by }\rho.
}
\]
